<Author>stace2007
<Content>Please Read this before you stay First I will say that this could be an excellent or a terrible based on what you are looking for.The first thing that you should know is that all of the balconies for the rooms are not open. The ocean view room balconies are open, but not the mountain view. I was initially assigned a mountain view, but after noting that the windows were filthy and there was a board across the window so there really was no appreciable view, I determined the room was not acceptable for what I was looking for.Initially I was told that I had been upgraded to the executive floor (which looked just like all of the other floors) and had a King Mountain View room with no working balcony. Note- this was nowhere on their web site. I asked for a room with a different balcony, and after several minutes of searching, the desk representative told me there were absolutely no other rooms and I should try back later in the week.After seeing the room I determined that I would not stay there the entire week. I am a Hilton fan and a Silver member and I love Hiltons, but I would have switched to another hotel completely. Upon returning to the front desk I asked when another room would be available and was told that they could switch me right then ( a different representative was helping me).I did not like having my first inquiry blown off, but I did end up with a nicely appointed ocean view room. It had two double beds instead of one king, but what the heck.I loved the room and the bathroom. If you leave the bathroom blinds open, you can actually see the ocean while in the shower. Maybe that's TMI, but I loved it. The room was immaculate and housekeeping was superbly professional. They always greeted me in the hallways and elevators and inquired about my stay. They would even get off of an elevator if they had a cart to allow guests to enter which was refreshing. I saw this happen repeatedly, so it must be policy. Bravo to Hilton Housekeeping Staff for their professionalism and attention to detail!The pool is on the 10th floor and is rarely, if ever, crowded. It's very windy, but that helps to keep the heat at bay.I wasn't impressed with the restaurant at all. I did not find the selection, quality or customer service to be of Hilton quality. They are very friendly, but no matter how empty or busy they were, they took forever to take my order, prepare the food, and getting the bill was actually painful. The lobby and lobby bar are decorated very nicely. The area, however, is not air conditioned and it is a closed lobby. That made it very stuffy and not a good place to sit and relax or wait for others to join you.I requested late check out and was told it was not available without even being asked how late of a check out I needed (it was only an hour). I asked about courtesy room and was told to check back the next morning when I needed one. I didn't end up using one, because had it not been available, it would have been too late to make other plans.The hotel is not right on the beach, but is within easy walking distance. You can also walk to the International Marketplace, the zoo, the aquarium, and many, many restaurants. There are at least 5 convenience stores within walking distance.If you plan on sending post cards, bring your own stamps. There is a machine that charges a very inflated price for them in the hotel store, but they will not change bills to provide you with change to use the machine and nobody seemed to know where a post office was located. All in all, I probably wouldn't stay here again, but it may be absolutely perfect for others.

<Author>InquisitiveTraveler
<Content>Cool design, friendly service We only stayed at this hotel for one night (6/22), prior to taking a cruise, but we really enjoyed it. The hotel has just been renovated, and the design of the rooms was great, (we loved the flat panel TVs, and the bathroom design was really cool). It also helped that we had a corner room on the 26th floor, with a view of the beach and DiamondHead from the balcony. It was about two blocks to the beach, and a very easy walk. Service was very friendly and helpful at the reception desk. Check-in was quick and easy. I didn't see a concierge when we were there, but the desk attendants were very helpful with restaurant recommendations. The only small problem with service we had was in the restaurant at lunch/brunch on Saturday. I guess they didn't really have enough people working, and were trying to seat everyone in one small section. All of the tables were full there, and so they were trying to get people to sit at the bar, which we really didn't want to do. After we complained, someone did finally ask a manager, who let us sit in another section. It took the waiter a while to get to us, but after he finally did things went better, and the food was really good(the pancakes are ENORMOUS).All in all an excellent stay, and I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>seayou99
<Content>Nice Hotel but wait for all renovations to be complete. Stayed here the last week in June on business. The place used to be a Radisson but I believe now that it is a Hitlon it is undergoing renovations. The rooms have a modern/contemporary decor and the beds were very comfortable. The best feature were the 42 in LCD hign def TVs in the rooms with a wide selection of movies. One night the cable TV went out so I was able to watch a movie (ppv) on the house. The one odd thing is that wall seemed exceptionally thin in that I could hear a lot of noise from the neighboring rooms and hallways. Another thing is the bathroom has no bath, only an oversized shower. The location is at the end of Waikiki about block from the beach and within walking distance of most dining and shopping opportunities the area has to offer. It is valet only parking (common to Waikiki) for about 20 bucks a day. My main gripe is that since they are still in the process of renovation, the first dozen or so floors are closed off. As a result, you have to take a separate elevator to the pool area (10th floor) which is quite inconvenient. In summary once these renovations are complete it should be a great hotel.

<Author>surfchic
<Content>Stayed here when it was a Radisson but disappointed now it is a Hilton Every spring we come to Hawaii and stay at the Prince Kuhio. We were very disappointed in our rooms and the restaurant. We booked an oceanview room and when we arrived they told us that the lanais were closed off because of the remodeling. The travel agency that I dealt with had no idea that we would not be able to access the lanai ( balcony ). With our ocean view room we had free breakfast every day. With the old Radisson Prince Kuhio we had a beautiful breakfast buffet every morning. This year we also had free breakfast. However, this new restaurant only gave you 2 choices for breakfast- either a fruit parfait or an american breakfast ( eggs, meat, toast or potatoes ). The staff here are still very polite. I did speak to several staff we knew from past years and they are not happy with the changes. They told us returning customers like myself will not return again. Now, about the rooms. They are smaller than they used to be and there is absolutely no drawer space for your clothes. The bathrooms are very cutesy but I don't live in a hotel bathroom when I am at the beach. I have to admit the beds were extremely comfortable. They have a 42 inch plasma T.V. but we thought the reception was not that great. In conclusion, I would rather stay at the Outrigger on the beach or the Sheraton . You are paying about the same price and the Prince Kuhio is 2 blocks back from the beach.

<Content>Don't worry about the old reviews We just returned from staying at the Hilton Prince Kuhio. Yes, they are still renovating and changing over from a Radisson to a Hilton property. We stayed on the 25th floor with an ocean view. The balconies are still closed due to outside renovations which was a disappointment. The renovations are very nice. We stayed at the same hotel 4 years ago and things are completely changed. The room is very nice and clean. The bathroom is all new with ceramic tile, glass shelving, big shower, plenty of towels. There's a plasma tv in the room, small fridge. The beds are comfortable but only double-sized. The staff was very helpful in giving us a late check-out and storing our luggage because of a late flight. They also gave us a courtesy room for an hour to get ready and change before we left for the airport. The package we had included a breakfast at their restaurant Mac 24/7. The staff are very friendly and helpful there, even learning our names and preferences during our stay. The one drawback was the free breakfast was limited to only a couple of choices but you can order from the menu (a little expensive but large portions). The hotel is located one block from the beach and on a main street (Kuhio) with a bus stop close by. Overall, a good experience. We talked to other travellers at other hotels and they would mention the worn or out-dated surroundings. We felt quite happy being in a newly renovated room. No problems with staying again.

<Author>acking
<Content>3rd time is a charm As a frequent business traveler, this is the 3rd time i have been to Hawaii since July. Every visit has forced me to stay at a different hotel, because of availability. This is the 2nd Hilton chain that I have spent a week in. This is much better and more convienient then the first. The second hotel should be refered to as a 1 star, although a high end 1 star hotel. I found the staff at the Prince Kuhio extremely professional, friendly and helpful. The valet staff was eager, energetic and responded quickly to arriving and departing customers. The counter staff addressed customers before they had to wait at the counter and as in most hotels I have stayed in, NEVER talked negatively about management and co-workers with hotel patrons within earshot. The staff at the lobby bar was phenominal. They went as far as to invent a drink for one of my travelling partners, because she was looking for something new. The rooms were always clean and the housekeeping staff, I found out late in my stay, was very creative, when then left a dog, fashioned from a large bath towel on my bed. The bathroom was newly remodeled and nice. The only concern I have is that the shower door leaked on the floor at the point where the hinge connects to the wall. I should have said something, but forgot until I began typing this. I had 2 travellers with me, and the staff ensured that not only we were on the same floor but in 3 rooms right next to one another. I found the laundry facilities convienient, clean and reasonable priced. The balcony was closed and the slider locked, but being in the construction industry, I understand the need to complete renovations and remain open for business. The noise was never an issue, because it was always at the end of the day when I heard it, and not something that would have offended me anyway. Overall, the hotel was great, and I will make every attempt to stay there again, when I return to Honolulu in February 07.The staff should disregard all the negative comments and remember that you are providing a great service in a time where upgrades and updates are being completed. I hope that during my next visit the hotel will be completed so I can see the finished product. I like what I see so far.

<Content>Beware Ventilation / Air Quality Issues We had originally intended to stay 5 nights at this hotel which is just a couple of blocks from Waikiki beach and offers a great view of the surf. <Author>vistatraveler
<Content>Some positives, some negatives My husband, teen son, and I stayed for a week at this hotel. We had no problems with the elevators and found that it was convenient to shopping and a short walk to the beach. However, when other reviewers said that the bathrooms were small, I never imagined how small they would be...VERY SMALL. Laying in bed it sounded like I was on the sidewalk of a busy city. The view from the balcony was beautiful though and the employees were helpful and friendly. Unfortunately, the price of parking went up to $20/day, which I had not known in advance. Next time, I'd stay in a hotel right across the street from Waikiki beach where there is still access to shopping and I could watch my son surf from the balcony.

<Content>Used to love the Radisson... My husband and I stayed at the Radisson four times over the past several years, and kept going back because our first two visits were wonderful. This was before they started renovations and apparently changed owners. The lobby used to be a comfortable-yet-dated place to hang out with a huge seating area and a tiny little bar staffed by very friendly bartenders. They have since renovated the lobby and changed it into a slightly less comfortable seating area with a kind of snooty bar, and moved all the friendly bar staff up to the pool bar.The rooms were always clean and well-tended, which is our number one concern -- we don't like to feel like we have to wear shoes in our room. During our last visit, however, we had drainage problems in the shower and there was a weird film over our mirror that staff said was just a part of the aging process, and that the room would eventually be renovated anyway. Plus, due to renovations, several elevators were out of service. They had a small sign up asking that people on the lower floors use the service elevators. We never saw the sign until our last day, and then it just left a bad taste in our mouths.Since changing owners, there seems to have been a change in the atmosphere. Although staff is still relatively polite, they used to be so much warmer and more attentive. We definitely felt the change on our third visit, and after our fourth visit decided it was time to start looking at other hotels in the same price category. Someone who has never been to this Radisson, or who is used to staying in lower-class hotels, will probably be comfortable and not disappointed with their trip, so it's a safe bet for a new traveller. We took my parents on this trip, and they were satisfied but spent time looking at other hotels while they were there to plan for their next trip.  
<Date>Jul 25, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great value, Excellent Hotel, Expensive Parking Stayed here 7 nights for our honeymoon. Location is great, within walking distance of everything in Waikiki, and is two blocks from beach. Room was midsized, clean, and the balcony was good, though small. Since we ended up with a city-view 4th fl room, we didn't hang out at the balcony very much. Hotel is being renovated, and we stayed in one of the not-yet-renovated rooms. It was average, with nothing to complain about really, except that I wish we had gotten one of the renovated rooms. Lobby staff was sometimes friendly and sometimes not, but always very helpful. The maintenance and maid staff was extremely friendly and helpful. Outdoor pool on the 10th floor was nice, though quite windy--don't carry bunch of stuff that may fly away there. We went to the pool at least once per day. Workout center is great as equipment is fairly new and advanced. Only one thing rubbed me the wrong way--$20 / 24hrs for valet or self parking. They do allow you to go in and out in the 24hr period as often as you like, however. We took advantage of that. Parking isn't cheap in Waikiki anyway, and you might as well park here rather than park a few blocks away to save $10, and have your car broken in or stolen.

<Content>Great Location Just returned from the Radisson Prince Kuhio. It is a very comfortable hotel. We had an ocean front room on the 17th floor with a great view of Waikiki Beach. My only complaints about the rooms would be the very small bathrooms (the shower/tub was very strange-had to step up into it, so it made the ceiling very low), and the bed was very hard. They advertise that they have the sleep number beds (which I have at home, so I was looking forward to a comfortable bed).....but they don't. At least not in the room that I had. They have renovated some of the rooms, so maybe they just hadn't gotten to our floor yet. I heard while we were there that the hotel was just bought by Hilton, so I don't know how this will affect anything. This is the 2nd time I have stayed at this hotel and I would definitely stay here again. It has been a few years since I have been to Waikiki, and it has gotten so crowded everywhere. Next time I would not go in the summer, or near a holiday (4th of July).

<Author>ReviewDC
<Content>Should be better next year The hotel is about two blocks from Waikiki beach. You can walk to the beach easily. And it was close to a lot of shops and restaurant, so it was convenient.The hotel is under renovation right now, so part of the hotel was closed from outside near the front entrance. We were dropped off by the shuttle bus from the airpot at the front entrance. The entrance is somewhat handicap accessible. Since we had suitcases, I rolled the suitcases up to front entrance. But inside the front entrance, the hotel only had stairs. Someone with wheel chair would not be able to get into the hotel at all. And I thought it was a very bad design for a hotel where most travelers are using suitcases with wheels.The lobby looks nice. The check in time was 3 o'clock in the afternoon. We got there around 2 and was asked to wait in the lobby for the room to be ready. While we were waiting, we picked up the pamphlet in the lobby. In the pamphlet, it states that all the rooms has 42 plasma TV. We were quite excited about that. When we got to our room, we didn't find the 42 plasma TV. When we called the operator, we were told that only the newly renovated rooms has the plasma TV. The room was small but clean. It has a small fridge with a bottle water in it. It also has a small balcony. We sat there for a while, but was bothered by the street noises. The hotel provided soap, shampoo, conditioner and shower cap. We reserved a room with ocean view. We were placed on the 21st floor. We were able to see the Waikiki beach from our room, although there is a tall building in front of the hotel, right in the middle of our view.We didn't go to the pool in the hotel but we went to check it out. It has a small pool with a lot of pool chairs. The pool is located on the 10th floor, so it doesn't really have any view. Overall, the hotel is good place to stay near Waikiki beach. But it should be even nicer after they are done with all the renovations.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Still nice, but should be better after rennovatins We are currently doing a 3 week tour of Hawaii, from the UK: first stop was this hotel for 3 nights. We had stayed there 2 years previously, and really liked it. We like the Kuhio Club level rooms, as they are at the top of the hotel, and the lounge with continental breakfast, and evening snacks is really nice. We booked the room through expedia and got a good rate. We were aware through the hotel's website about the room rennovations, but did not know how they would affect us.Here's what we made of the hotel:1) Location - we like the location towards the diamond head end of waikiki (quieter) and its just one block away from the beach2) Parking - they are still rennovating the entrance to the hotel (as they were 2 years ago!) so the entrance is to the side of the hotel and there is only valet parking ($12/night) - they are were quick at loading and unloading our luggage and car was brought quickly each day3) Lobby - new lobby nice, more modern than previously, however air conditioning seemed to be not working so was a bit stuffy sonetimes!4) Check-in- staff not overly friendly and we were not informed of the rennovations. Were checked into top floor 37. Was apparant that they are rennovating all floors from 36 down to 24 currently.5) Room - bright, adequate, and clean, but def showing age. Small but functional bathrroom. Had nice view of ocean and diamond head from balcony.6) Kuhio Lounge - no chages from 2 years ago. Relaxed, friendly service, good continental breakfast and evening hot and appetizers. 7) Elevators - new lifts now faster so no problems waiting as previously8) Rennovations - the hotel is way behind schedule. They have blocked out floors 24 to 36 but when we were there they were working on floor 36 (just one below the top floor). On the Monday we were woken up by loud drilling and hammering in the room below. The workmen left the doors open so we could look over and see them working on the floor below. They are working from 9-4pm Mon - Fri. Despite apologies from the front desk we were told that no aleternative rooms were available. They really should close the Kuhio club floor temporarily and rennoavte that rather than leave it open. It seems that the hotel wants to get the extra bucks by keeping this floor open, but this is not acceptable while they are working on the floor below. The front desk should also have warned us that we could be disturbed by such loud noise.The man in the club was not sure when the top floor would be done, and no-one was sure when the nerw rooms would be available. From the amount of noise and the display in the lobby it seems that the rooms are being completely gutted out and totally new baths with separte shower, bath, new beds and flat screen plasma tvs. This hotel should be awesome when these rooms are available, but right now I would avoid it until these are available. If I was staying there soon (particulalry the Club level) I would contact the hotel to check on progress of rennovations, and ensure that I was not on floor 37.Please see my review about the Grand Wailea Hotel, on Maui - our next stop!

<Content>Enhanced A Great Vacation The hotel enhanced our vacation as we celebrated our 4th anniversary. All the literature I read on the hotel stated it was being renovated. The hotel is beautiful: an elegantly appealing lobby, alluring tropical garden, great dining in the Trellis Restaurant, and business center with 4 computers/printer/copy machine. Although not on the beach, it is only one long block from it and the walk is pleasant. An ABC Store (1 of about 40 in Waikiki) is located diagnally across from the hotel which made it convenient for soda, suntan lotion, gifts for back home, etc. The ONLY negatives we thought mentioning was that the pool is on the 10th floor and it was super windy that high up. Also (a minor item) the TV did not allow hooking up my camcorder to view the scenes I had taped during the day. Parking was $12 a day with ample parking spaces. We parked on the 7th floor parking, so we just walked into the hallway to our room. (The garage door-to-hallway was not locked during the day, but was secured around 7 pm.) We will not hesitate to stay here again on our next vacation to Hawaii.  
<Date>Apr 27, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Love Hawaii, even in the rain!! We stayed in this hotel March 11th - 17th. I found the staff very friendly and helpful. Had some minor problems 1)one of the keys we received did not work and took awhile to get another one. 2)There was water on the carpet right outside of the bathroom and did not know where it was coming from. We were moved to a different room immediately. Other than these small issues I thought it was great. Location is wonderful. So close to everything, a pleasant short walk to the beach and it's surrounded by restaurants and shops. Felt very comfortable letting my teenage son go out on his own at night. Very nice area. Our room overlooked the garden and pond which was nice. The hotel is far enough from the busy traffic of Kalakaua Ave. that it was very quiet at night. Did not have the breakfast buffet but did have a very good breakfast our first morning there. Did not have a car and did not miss having one. All of our tours provided pickup at the hotel and I was glad to let someone who knew where they were going fight the traffic. Enjoyed our stay at this hotel very much and would go back. Rain was somewhat of a problem but not enough to interfere with activities. Cool and breezy in evenings. Paradise Cove Lu'au was wonderful but wish I had taken a sweater. Fortunately for us, heavy rains and sewer overflows were the following week. Would hesitate however to visit Hawaii in March again. Would definately go at a time when the whales are there. Highly recommend Dolphin Excursions. We took a boat out on 3/16 to the westside just below the north shore and ended up in the middle of a pod of humpbacks. We sighted at least 8 to 10 males chasing a female. The marine biologist was very informative and the boat ride was a blast. They stopped so we could snorkel on the way back and the water was crystal clear with tons of colorful fish. This was the highlight of the week. Also highly recommend Discover Hawaii Tours. The Circle Island tour was great. Tour guides were very friendly and informative. Stopped and allow plenty of time at each point of interest. Lunch at the Ko'Olau Golf Club was a treat. Food's so-so but scenery is incredible. This Texan is in love with Hawaii!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel I gave my husband a trip to Hawaii for Christmas. I booked everything on Expedia for a little under $2000. This included an ocean view room from Monday to Saturday, a rental car, and the airfare on Hawaiian Airlines. We got to the hotel before checkin time, but they were still able to give us our room. The staff at the front desk was so nice and the lobby is exactly as pictured from Expedia. The hotel is less than a 5 minute walk from the beach and there were a lot of little convenience stores around if you forget that little something. We got to our room and the ocean view is something that I think is a must when staying in Hawaii. It was a great view. There was one hotel blocking our view just a bit, but we could still see most of the ocean. Also, if we looked out to our left we could see Diamond Head which was a pleasant surprise. There was ample parking, but keep in mind that we had to pay $12 per day for parking. This is about average for the hotels around there. You could travel by bus or trolley, but there's nothing like the freedom of going where you want, when you want. The hotel also provided us with a free breakfast buffet every morning. This was not just any old continental buffet. They had eggs, bacon, french toast, bagels, and all sorts of fruit. The staff at the restaurant was also very friendly. Actually everyone in Hawaii was generally helpful and friendly to the tourists. I would speak more about all the activities to do around the area, but unfortunatly it rained about 95% of the time we were there. Not only that, but they happend to have the worst sewage spill on the day that we got there and they said you could go in the water at your own risk. Of course, I didn't even attempt to put on my bathing suit because it rained the entire time. We did look at the pool which seemed nice and would have probably been really nice to take a dip in, but then again there was the rain. Basically I loved the location of the hotel, the staff was great and our room was great. There was a fridge in the room and a coffee maker. We had a little balcony which was great too look at. Since we experienced all the rain my husband and I decided that we had to come back again. Next time we had to make sure the weather would be nothing but sunny skies. The only reason I didn't give the hotel 5 stars was because the hotel is not exactly next to the beach and we had to pay for parking. Other than that the hotel was great. Keep in mind that if you do choose a hotel on the beach you are bound to pay much much more than we did. We decided that the ocean view and the 5 minute walk was worth saving some bucks.

<Author>AlaskaFlamingo
<Content>Loved the Prince Kuhio Radisson Horel Our travel agent suggested this hotel and apologized for it being only 3 stars. Needless to say, we had low expectations especially after we read other Travel Advisor reports about the hotel, but what the heck - we were going to be on the beach everyday!Boy, were we in for a treat. The hotel was lovely, the staff was very friendly and helpful and the food was terrific. Breakfast buffet was a part of our package, much to our surprise and delight, and the food was well prepared and plentiful and catered to a variety of cultures. Rice, both white and fried; potato pancakes; bagels; lots of fresh fruit and 5-6 melon choices; egg choice was changed daily from basic scrambled to Eggs Benedict to Eggs Florentine. Bacon, Sausage and ham were often the meat choices. At least 4 juice choices as well as teas, coffee and milk for beverages. Bread for toast, croissants, danish pastry etc and the list goes on.Our reservation was for an ocean view room with a king bed and when we checked in we had an ocean view room with 2 queens. When I brought this to the clerk's attention she promptly switched us to what we wanted - no if's, and's or but's about it and it was 1 o'clock in the morning! This hotel is about 2 blocks from the beach and on a main bus route so getting around town was pretty easy.The room was very comfortably and clean. The linae was tiny but did accommodate 2 chairs and a small table and since we don't do heights and were on the 33rd floor, it was fine with us. TV with cable and pay-per-view stations, nice dresser and 2 night stands with deep drawers. Coffee pot and complimentary Kona Coffee-both regular and decaf. More than 1 packet of each would have been nice but not a big deal and hardly worth mentioning. Plenty of towels in the bathroom. Internet is available in the room for about $10 per day plus tax, but is complimentary in the Business Center in the lobby.The pool is 6' deep and not very large but suited our needs. The bar has favorite beverages-both alcoholic and non and a variety of snacks. Lots of lounge chairs and plenty of towels AND a hot tub for 4-6.This is a security hotel and you need your room key to get the elevators to operate and to get to the pool area. We found this an added benefit.We did use the tour reservations people in the lobby and found them to be very knowledgeable and they put together what we wanted very quickly. The woman even knew which public bus would get us to a variety of locations ;-) All in all we were very happy with our stay at the Radisson Prince Kuhio.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Place! My husband and I just returned from Hawaii. We had spent 3 nights in Wikiki at the Radisson Prince Kuhio. I was very impressed with the hotel. Upon checking in, we were upgraded to a better room with no additional charge. THe lobby was very nice and it wasn't as noisey as the main strip. The location was great (a block from the beach), the service was good, and the staff was friendly. The pool on the tenth floor served its purpose and the hot tub was a bonus! The pool was opened late and it had a bar/snack bar too. My only complaint is that if you are on the lower floors (I was on the 11th), you hear the buses early in the morning. I am an early bird on vacation, but when I wanted to sleep until 7:00-7:30, I couldn't b/c you could clearly hear the loud buses and traffic. If you don't mind this, then you are set. But if you like to sleep a little late, I advise staying on one of the higher floors if your on the ocean side. Great hotel, clean, and highly recommended. I would definitely stay there again!

<Author>Yung4fr
<Content>Convenient yet quiet location My husband and I stayed 4 nights at the Radisson in February 2006.Hotel is towards the Diamond Head end of Waikiki and a long block from the beach (this means a short block to Ala Wai Blvd and close to Kapahulu which facilitates fast exit from Waikiki.) I like the location -- short 5-10 minutes walk to the heart of Waikiki, but away from the noise and hustle.Only got a mountain-view room on 11th floor due to the relatively low corporate rate I used. In general, we don spend much time in the room and hardly ever out on the lanai so view is not a requirement for us. Room is spacious enough. Lanai is small with only enough space for 2 chairs and a little table, but adequate if you like to relax there for a cup of coffee in the morning (when it is not too windy, otherwise it's a great place to dry your wet swimsuits). TV, mini fridge, coffee maker, hair dryer, ironing board and iron, room safe ($3 extra per day), 2 phones and high speed internet. USA Today was delievered to the room daily (not sure if that's because this is part of the corporate rate package), and Star Bulletin (local paper) was available in the hallway for you to take. Bed was comfortable; they will be renovating and switching over to sleep number beds later this year, which should be even better. Room is clean, but things are showing signs of age (e.g. old carpeting). Bath room is small so both people could not get ready together in it, but there is a sink and mirror outside the bathroom where the coffee maker counter is. Soap, shampoo, conditioner, body lotion, and shower caps are provided amenities. There is also a clothing line in the bathroom over the tub. Pool area (on 10th floor) is not large, and was shaded most of the morning and quite windy, but that posed no problems to us since we primarily went there to pick up towels for the beach. The hot tub was very warm, in fact I think it was a little too warm to use during the day (or was it because I was a little sun burnt?). I sat on the steps in the pool one morning relaxing and reading newspaper, and the water seems to be heated? Well, it did not feel cold, so I am assuming that it must be heated.We never had long waits for the elevators. The lobby was spacious. The car entrance to the hotel was a little difficult to find and I think a more prominent sign would have been helpful. The employees are very nice and friendly.Overall I think the hotel is worth the price I paid, and I am very happy with it and will stay there again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Convient location/Mildew in the walls (includes Oahu tips) My husband and I stayed in a partial ocean-view room for two nights. The hotel is conviently located near the International Junk/Marketplace and the beach. Take a walk just a bit further down, and find a cleaner (and quieter) beach. Or, better yet, go to Hanauma Bay (more on that later). The staff was very friendly. When we arrived, we were told that they had little information about our needs (we had booked on Priceline, and had been quoted for a room with one king or two double-beds). They were able to accomodate us in a non-smoking, double-bed room with a partial-ocean view. When we walked into the room, we noticed that there was a mildewy smell which we thought was related to the air conditioning. We should have asked to change rooms, but thought that if we slept without the a/c on, we would be o.k. BIG MISTAKE. Since this was the last day of our trip, we didn't change rooms but returned home with a chest cold/infection from the mold. We were miserable.The hotel is undergoing construction and should be ready by this fall (2006). I'm sure the rooms will be much nicer at that time, because they are extremely outdated now. We also stayed at the Outrigger Reef and the Hilton Hawaiian Village, the latter of the two being the best. I don't know if other rooms at the Radisson had the mildew problem, but noise (ocean-view is also street-side) is also a concern. A few highlights for your trip:- Sam Choy's restaurant is AMAZING for a fine dining experience (Pacific Rim cuisine)- Visit 'Leonard's Bakery' for fresh, hot malasadas (Portugese pastries)- Seabird Tours - coupon in 'Best of Oahu' (pick up at concierge desk or in lobby) for $12 round trip transport and gear to snorkel at Hanauma Bay- Polynesian Cultural Center - don't spend extra for the 'Ambassador' package unless you can't navigate yourself around a theme park; don't take a tour with Rob (Samoa)- Paradise Cove luau is MUCH better than the one at the Polynesian Cultural Center, or anywhere else!- Chinatown is a lot of fun for an afternoon walk or for a photo-shoot- Go to Hanauma Bay early, early in the morning (otherwise the water becomes cloudy from swimmers)- Take a hike with 'Oahu Nature Tours' - Mike, the owner, is extremely knowledgeable and helpfulHave a wonderful time! Aloha!

<Author>Member05
<Content>Location as Convenient as Expected For the price, this was one of the most convenient hotels to stay in. It is on Kuhio, 1 block back from the beach and walking distance to just about everything you would want from Waikiki beach. There are plenty of beaches to choose from to lounge on. Pleanty of eateries, shops, department/apparel/designer stores. However, you will be on the very end of the wakiki strip near Kapiolani park. I found that I did not need anything from the other end, which is close to the convention center, so this was not a problem for me. If anything, I found it a great opportunity to take a nice stroll along the beaches or Ala Wai Blvd (which is where most of the shops are). As for the hotel in detail:1 - the cleanliness was average to below average. I would say 3 star is accurate. Everything that could be taken care of on a daily basis was done very well: clean sheets, clean towels, good overall room cleaning. But the carpet in general is very old. 2 - the elevators were super slow. At first I didn't notice a thing until the weekend came and then I noticed the inconvenience of the 2 elevators being repaired. However, they inform guests on signs that they should use the service elevators so in the end, we weren't inconvenienced too much over the course of our 5 nights.3 - the room that we were in on I believe the 7th floor was SUPER windy. It was impossible for me to sit out on the balcony. We still left the door open for fresh beach air, but it did get pretty noisy. 4 - the actual location itself is not very noisy and I didn't feel disrupted at all by crowds, probably b/c the hotel is on the street behind the main street.Summary: great deal for great location. Staff was also very nice.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Oahu, not as advertised !!!! Most of us would probably consider Hawaii high on the short list of the world ultimate tropical vacation destinations. My perspective is of course tempered by our other travels to similar destinations. Value is different to different people depending on your experiences and expectations. Perhaps that is why we read these reviews, to fill in the blanks that exist in our own experiences.Keep this in mind as you read on. We have traveled a great deal in the Caribbean. We find cruise ships and all-inclusive resorts the best value available today by a long shot. For those of you who do not know, true all-inclusives do not exist in the United States. This is due to the obvious high labor costs and countless other restrictive American labor laws. In Hawaii most of the hotels like to call themselves esorts? they are not, they are just hotels.If there is an opposite of all-inclusive, I not sure what we would call it, but Hawaii would be a text book example of it. Our stay was at the Radisson Prince Kuhio on Waikiki for the Pro-Bowl in February 2006. Clean, outstanding staff, well organized hotel. However, at the $250 per day neighborhood you would think something besides a bed would be included. We were disappointed to find an extra charge for nearly everything. $12 per day to park your car there, $3 per day if you use the safe in the room, and $1 per local phone call, even if it a toll-free number ! Very noisy all night even with the balcony door closed on upper floors.Waikiki beach has long been considered by many to be among the best beaches in the world. Sorry, but we are beach people and have been to many that are high on the list . Waikiki is narrow, very crowded, noisy, and the sand is mostly ground up sea shells. The sand therefore does not pack or knit together and is hard to walk in near the water line for long distances. This was what we found in most of Oahu. Also a lot of rocks everywhere except in a few developed areas in front of major hotels. There appears to be no effort by officials to get rid of dirty homeless people laying around 24/7. I know this is part of the urban scene, but they should not be allowed to live on the streets and beaches of areas like this. (This is rarely seen on developed Caribbean beaches where they are supposedly much poorer).Unless you have lots of money to waste on over-priced tours, you will need to rent a car. Alamo was $150 for 4 days, good service, nice car. However Oahu highways are in near total gridlock nearly all day, everywhere! Even out away from the urban areas. The entire island is overdeveloped, and crowded, and there lots more major tourism development on the way. Sorry, not my definition of paradise.

<Author>soxgal78
<Content>Good for what we needed My boyfriend and I stayed at the Prince Kuhio Jan. 24-26, 2006. All in all, I think it was a good pick for us. We weren't really into the Waikiki scene, so it was nice to be a bit away from all the busy traffic, shops, etc., but still within easy walking distance to go grab a beer at Duke's and hit the beach. The room and bathroom were pretty standard. No view for us--we opted to spend more on our stay on Maui than in Honolulu--but from what I could tell, I'm guessing it was pretty nice.FYI: the gym was under renovation while we were there, so the front desk (always very nice and accommodating) gave us free passes to use the 24-Hour Fitness club across the street at the Pacific Beach Hotel. Great gym, all new equipment and plenty of it -- just make sure to bring your own towel because they charge you for one of theirs. The breakfast buffet was complimentary for us, though not apparently for everyone (we were behind one group in line in which two people had comp breakfast tickets and two didn't). I wouldn't spend the $14.95 for it if you don't -- there's a decent variety of food to choose from, but none of it too outstanding. It was nice to be able to grab something quickly before heading out, though.We liked the pool, though it was a bit windy up on the 10th floor. The bar drink deals were great for a lazy happy hour, though!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Radisson ok, probably better after renovations are compelete My husband and I stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio Nov. 2-9, 2005. We rented a car at the airport and drove to Waikiki. We had a difficult time finding the entrance to the hotel. After driving past it 3 times, we finally saw the entrance to the parking garage. Very frustrating after a long trip. The hotel staff was very courteous, the lobby and bar were very comfortable. Our room was ok, but the bathroom was very cramped. The bathtub did not drain very well and it was difficult getting in and out as the toilet was less the 8 inches from the tub. Our room overlooked the garden behind the hotel and the mountain breezes were very pleasant. We elected to turn off the air conditioner and keep the doorwall open while we slept. The breakfast buffet was great and a good value for the amount and variety of foods that were available. Two of the elevators were out of service while we were there so at times there was a long wait. The beach was only 1.5 blocks away and a nice walk. Since we didn't spend much time in our room other than to sleep, shower and dress, it proved to be a good value. Being a block and a half away from the beach also kept the noise level down. The concierge was a great help to us by providing maps, directions and ideas for places to go and things to see. I would probably stay there again once the renovations are complete.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Stay My fiancee and I stayed at the Radisson Waikiki in late December 2005 for our wedding/honeymoon and had a wonderful experience. I researched hotels in and around the beach for hours and finally decided on the Radisson because of the value for our dollars and the nice location (only a block away from the beach, which was close enough to walk, but far enough from all the hub-bub to feel secluded). We reserved an Ocean-View room, and got a reasonable deal on it. I made sure to call ahead to let the staff know it would be a special occasion for us. When we arrived, they arranged for us to have a room on the 37th floor, which had a spectacular view of the beach. They also gave us free breakfast buffet passes for our entire stay, and gave us a pass for a free bottle of champagne. These were very nice small touches that meant a lot to us. We found the staff, from the valets, to the receptionists, to the restaurant staff, to all be helpful and pleasant. The breakfast buffet at Trelliss's was also really good and had all the staples (eggs, pancakes, hashbrowns, sausage, french toast, etc), which I didn't grow tired of during our stay. The room itself was basic, but clean, with nice furniture, and a great balcony. We found we had enough space to spread out. I also never heard anyone else in the rooms around us, which was nice. I didn't find the bathroom to be too small, which seemed to be a common complaint among the various hotel reviews. Not much else to add, except that we would definitely stay at Radisson again.By the way, note that the hotel advertised that it would be undergoing room renovations through Fall 2006.Take it or leave it...one couple's thoughts. P.S. We'd recommend Hula Grill as a good place to eat, and be sure to ask for directions to the local bakery that sells malasatas (puff pastrys dipped in sugar).  
<Date>Jan 20, 2006

<Author>coffee01
<Content>Could do better... We stayed at this hotel for 2 weeks in December and were disappointed with what we found. The rooms are a reasonable size, but the bathrooms are tiny and the toilet in ours had leaked water from around the base (which smelled) - once in regular use, this leak stopped, but it wasn't a good start. The toilet in the courtesy room that we used on our last day also leaked. The waste pipe from the bath was constantly backing up, and by the time you finished showering the bath was half full of water.The sound-proofing between rooms and between floors is non-existent. You can hear the person above walking across the room, and every time anyone flushes a toilet or runs a shower the noise is enough to wake the dead. Don't expect a good night's sleep unless you have earplugs.The second floor is being renovated, so the gym is closed. You can use 24/7 fitness just down the road and it's a good, well-equipped gym, but make sure you have photo ID (something reception probably won't tell you about when they issue your 'pass').Breakfast in the hotel was brilliant - everything you could possibly want to eat, but the evening meal was a different story. Unless you like 'smash' (reconstituted mashed potato), avoid the so-called 'garlic mash'. Not many people ate in the hotel whilst we were there and there was a lot of waste. Staff freely wandered in and out of the dining room picking at the buffet as they went - very hygenic!The bar in the lobby has been refurbished and this is a really nice area. The bar staff are friendly and happy, which made a pleasant change as most of the reception staff were surly and bordered on being rude.Hopefully the renovations will address some of the problems with the rooms, but at the present time I wouldn't recommend spending more than a few days in this hotel. It's not a good advert for the Radisson chain.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great for Business traveler I have stayed in many hotels on the island over the years, and this is the first one that I have desired to go back to. I travel for business, so of the more expensive hotels are not an option. The room was clean (a really clean hotel room in Waikiki is not the norm). I had an high speed internet connection in my room, as well as a free continental breakfast. It is only 2 blocks from the beach and a short drive to the H-1 (if you take the back road and avoid all the Waikiki traffic). The part I feel I cannot stress enough is the cleanliness. I am not quite a germaphobe, but I hate dirty hotel rooms. Any mold or unneccessary stains will cause me to change hotels (which I do often when I am displeased, changed hotels 3 times over a 2 week stay this month in Guam). I highlt recommend this hotel. Great views from all the rooms, a nice pool area, and only a nice block (open with shops, a starbucks, and a 24 hour fitness) from the beach.

<Author>nbell8
<Content>Nice hotel away from bustle We stayed here on our honeymoon for our 4 days in Oahu. We picked a cheaper place to stay in Oahu and splurged for a really nice beachfront hotel in Maui for our 2nd part of the honeymoon. We were glad we did. We were more impressed with the beaches in Maui than Waikiki. Waikiki is nice, but its not huge and can get crowded and noisy (compared to Maui). We had oceanview room (corner room so we had a wraparound balcony) and had very good view of Waikiki beach. We could see the surfers our at the crack of dawn waiting for the waves. We also had buffet breakfast included in room price. Its an OK buffet (not a huge selection of food), but nice service and closeby. The elevators were annoying (we were on the upper floor and had to deal with the lower floor people using our elevators instead of the 'service elevators'). I agree that the bathrooms were pretty small. You had to dance around the door to close it (it just cleared the toilet). Otherwise, it was a nice clean room and good size balcony and room. We weren't expecting a fancy place for the price. It was really a short walk to the beach and buses and there are nice places to walk around and restaurants (we loved the Hy Steakhouse which is 1-2 blocks away. The Mai Ti and cheesy bread were fabulous.) Also nice thing was hardley any kids at the hotel (unlike the beachfront ones where kids are running around screaming like nuts).

<Author>TNT123
<Content>A very nice hotel We travelled from Adelaide to Australia to get married on Maui. My new husband, 4 retired parents and myself then flew to Waikiki and stayed at the Radisson from 8th to 13th October 2005. We had oceanview rooms on the 17th, 24th and 27th floors and all of us were very impressed. I had read a lot of complaints about the lack of and slowness of lifts but we didn't find this to be a problem - on average we had a 1 minute wait. Our bedrooms were all the same and we found them to be very comfortable, clean and smart. Unless you are a very big person the size of the bathroom should be ample. The views from the balcony were superb.The location of this hotel is excellent - very close to the beach without overpowering tourists. We would definitely stay therel again.One of the highlights of our time on Oahu was Hanuama Bay - we arrived there at 7.45am and already there were quite a few people. The beach was excellent at this time, and worth going early. There was plenty of space when we left at 12pm but it felt more relaxed earlier in the morning. I snorkeled in relatively shallow water (120cm deep) and saw soooooo many different species of fish. We have holidayed on the Great Barrier Reef, Australia and Hanuama Bay was just as good for the amount of fish we saw. I had read other reviews noting they had seen very little fish, this was not the case for us.

<Author>mmmeyerisu
<Content>Well worth the $ I also agree with most of the reviews posted here that the Radisson is a solid choice. We stayed at the Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio the week of September 5th. We were on the 22nd floor with an ocean view room and it was a great scene every morning and evening. The hotel is a short walk to all the shops and restaurants in the area. The street outside can be just a little bit noisy but nothing like the other main streets which run by the hotels directly on the beach. We had no problems with the elevators as we could always use the service elevators near the other elevators. We did not use the pool since the ocean is a 3 minute walk away. Traffic in Honolulu is sloooow so if the event/place you are going offers a shuttle, take it! Also if you are going to the USS Arizona memorial get there and in line before 7:30am or you will not get on the boat out to the memorial until past noon.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not bad for price Before making my reservation i read all the reviews for this hotel. I will say that i have to agree with just about all the reviews i've read. The hotel was very nice, clean, and in a perfect location of waikiki. Your away from busy downtown but close enough to walk to it if you like. I had an ocean view room on the 26th floor that had a great view of the ocean. I spent lots of time on the balcony but if your afraid of heights you may want to consider a lower floor. The best thing that my family liked about the hotel is the full breakfast. They had everything you can imagine for breakfast. My son is 5 yrs old and he was up early every morning just to get downstairs to have breakfast. The breakfast was included in my package deal which i do recommend. Otherwise the breakfast buffet can get expensive. The beach is a little over a block away which takes you about 3 to 5 minutes to walk to. You can use the walk if you eat there breakfast every morning. The only complaint that i would have is that only 3 of the 5 elevators were out of service due to them upgrading them. I recommend to use the garage and service elevators since not very many people know about it. I can't use that against them, they are just trying to make the hotel better for all of us. Overall we were very satisfied with the hotel, service, and especially the location. If we return we will definately stay there again unless i start reading bad reviews on trip advisor.

<Author>U2fan
<Content>Nice hotel We stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio for four nights over the Labour Day weekend. We were in room 812, which overlooked Waikiki beach (the odd numbered rooms overlooked the canal / mountains, which still was a great view). The hotel is 37 floors, so the higher up you are, the better view you get. We took the lift up to the 37th floor and the views were AMAZING! The hotel was very comfortable - our room was large, and the air conditioning was excellent (coming from the UK, we really needed it!!!!!). We had a balcony but I'm scared of heights, so we didn't use it. We used the hotel's pool a couple of times - both times, it was fairly quiet. The staff in the pool bar were very friendly. The hotel's in a great location - it's only a few minutes walk to Waikiki beach but it's far enough away from all the madness! There's a convenient ABC store across the road. The only downside to the hotel was that three of the five lifts were out of service (being upgraded), which caused a few delays.

<Author>6andy6
<Content>Nice hotel set back from the hussle and bustle Nice hotel with large but fairly dark lobby looking onto a small courtyard garden. Bar in lobby and restaurant off with a souvenir/ convenience shop opening onto lobby. Room was on 16th floor looking oceanward - great view (given there is a vacant lot across the road and a church) and small balcony. Usually floral bedspreads amercians appear to love (but were in fashion in the 70's). Good size tv with good selection of cable and local channels and fridge. Others have said the rooms were small - I didnt think so and while not LARGE prob would be 20 or 25 sq. Pool area is on adjacent podium - pool medium size but surrounded by concrete and therefore can be a bit glary and hot during the day - there are some plants but this area could easily be remodeled into a tropical garden and so enhance the pool no end. Is usually fairly quiet to which is nice. Coffee shop - only had dinner there once and very nice set up with a buffet carvery one night. Parking garage ramps very steep and somewhat sharp.Set on Kuhio avenue the hotel overall is very pleasant and does not have the busy lobby that more central hotels on the beachfront have. Having said that - it is by no means remote and is only a 5 or 10 minute walk at most to the action. Would def stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>bolt the door Stayed at the Radisson for three nights in May. The hotel itself is very comfortable and the pool area is quite adequate with the pool and a hot jacuzzi open until midnight. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Immaculate, Great Location, Efficient Staff Stayed for two weeks. Reliable hotel - worth it if you get a good deal on the price. I usually prefer smaller hotels so will probably try the Ilima next time and make use of having a kitchen or perhaps if I have the bucks one of the Outriggers on the beach, but, as I was travelling with my teenage son and on a budget, this turned out to be a great choice with the all-you-can-eat breakfast buffet included in the price (which we never tired of), the pool area was a decent size - where families with young children also seemed well entertained, the mountainview from our room was lovely (hotel was too full to get an upgrade to ocean view) and the cleanliness of the entire hotel and friendliness of the staff made it very comfortable. The pool area had a good breeze which made suntanning very comfortable whereas the beach became too hot very quickly. The lobby was beautiful, rooms bright, tastefully decorated (okay, maybe the beige rooms were just a little bland) and nice marble bathrooms. Having read many reviews about the tiny bathrooms in other Waikiki hotels, I think these bathrooms were very nice in comparison. I also really liked the fact that at night this hotel's location felt very safe and quiet - being surrounded by other large hotels - Marriott, Pacific Beach and Banyan contributed to the calmer feel - travel a few blocks west on Kuhio (i.e. near Ohana East) and you'll run into much more noise and congestion (and a couple ladies of the night). The other plus at this hotel is the ample, easily accessible parking. Yes, they are rebuilding the elevators, leaving only three available, but I did not find the wait that big a deal or worth getting worked up about. This is not a luxury hotel but definately a big step up from budget and had everything we needed. Also found it worth having a rental car for 7 days and visited beautiful Kailua and Lanikai beaches on the windward side of the island and on the North Shore Turtle Beach and excellent snorkelling at Shark's Cove. Oahu Revealed is an excellent guide for these things.

<Author>manoloblahnik
<Content>Close to the beach and reasonably priced My friend and I stayed here for 4 days and the only complaint we have were the elevators. Only 2 of the 5 elevators were working so there was a substantial wait for the elevator, especially since there were 37 floors in the hotel. Other than that, the hotel was fine and had a really nice lobby and bar.The rooms were medium sized, not too big, not too small. We had the mountain view room which had a beautiful view of a lush green mountain, palm trees and houses. The mountain view rooms also come with a breakfast buffet which is very worthwhile for an extra $8/day on Expedia. It is not a contintental breakfast -- it is a FULL breakfast with poi pancakes, fresh sliced fruit, bacon, eggs benedict, etc... The menu changed daily. The hotel is only 1 block from the beach; a very easy walk. None of the hotels by the Radisson are on the beach (except the Hilton and Sheraton which are down the street), so if you book a room at another hotel thinking it's right on the beach, it's not. You still have to cross the street to get to the beach. Save the extra $50/night at these other hotels and walk a block to the beach.Another good thing about this hotel is that they offer a hospitality room if you have a late flight. You get the room for 1 hour to freshen up before you leave. Nice ending to a great stay.

<Author>GeoGirl
<Content>Excellent Waikiki hotel We stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio for the first half of our honeymoon, June 27-July 2nd and enjoyed everything about it. The staff was friendly and helpful and the room was a decent size and clean. We were on the 32nd floor and on the corner, so while our room was a Mountain View, our balcony wrapped around and we could see the ocean through the buildings (room 3219). Too bad we were too scared of the height to spend much time on there! The location was good, the breakfast buffet was very good, especially if it comes free with your room in a package. You can't really complain too much about free food, and there was a good variety. The restaurant otherwise was a bit dissapointing for the cost. Very slow service and just so-so food. The hotel is a quick walk to a nice part of Waikiki beach, and the location is quieter than some of the more central hotels. You can walk anywhere in Waikiki from the Radisson, so it is convenient and a bit nicer to be out of the throngs of people. The pool was really nice, and the loungers were very comfortable. The pitchers of Pina Colada's were some of the best we had. All in all this was a great hotel and we would definetely return!

<Content>Good Hotel Very nice hotel. Received a good deal with a package of a rental car. The room was nicely decorated and clean. Housekeeping did an excellent job. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Prince Kuhio Four of us went to the Prince Kuhio for spring break in March, and it was perfect for us. We are twenty something law students and stayed in one room and it was fine. The rooms are not huge, but have everything you need and are clean. We loved the pool, hot tub, and pool bar on the 7th floor so we would go the beach and come back there in the afternoon to relax before going to dinner and out for the night. The breakfast was EXCELLENT- probably some of the best food we ate in Oahu, and I highly recommend packages that offer the full breakfast with it. The staff was very friendly and the food was wonderful- fresh fruits, eggs, pancakes, etc.. we'd just eat there and then not really need a big lunch or anything. The only problem we had was with Expedia- we booked the package and paid extra for the breakfast and Expedia forgot to the tell the hotel that- but we resolved it over the phone and Expedia paid the hotel for our breakfasts.The hotel is close to everything in Waikiki and an easy walk to Diamondhead- it really is great even if its just a half block away from the beach. We walked in most of the hotels in Waikiki and liked this one the best by far for its price/value.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Loved the Radisson Prince Kuhio! My 11 year old son and I just got back from a week at the Radisson Prince Kuhio and we had a blast! We had a mountain room that included breakfast which was superb. There was fresh pineapple, melon, papaya, french toast, sausage or bacon, pancakes, scrambled eggs, a variety of eggs benedict/florentine, several varieties of granolo and other cereals, several kinds of juices and my own pot of coffee! Not sure what else you could ask for! The room was a good size, we had two double beds on the 15th floor, which was just high enough for a nice view. The pool area was really nice, with a poolside bar and grill, and nice wooden deck chairs in addition to the typical patio kind. We were in walking distance of Prince Kuhio beach, which was really nice and close to Waikiki beach center where you can take surf lessons and get a beach burger with fries or a plate lunch. We were also close to a Wolfgang Puck Express restaurant, which had a great selection of not only pizzas, but chicken, caesar and other salads, mac and cheese (Puck quality), which was great when we didn't want to go out to dinner, but wanted good quality food. All in all it was a fabulous time and we are planning on going back to the Prince Kuhio as soon as we can!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent for the price and location My wife, my 6 year old son and I stayed there from June 14-22. We were a little budget conscious but wanted to find a 3 star hotel at a good price. I read many reviews on other hotels on Waikiki for three star hotels and had the impression that a lot of them were old and run down. Three star hotels with stained carpets and dirty walls made me think that a decent 3 star hotel would be hard to find.The Radisson Prince Kuhio was outstanding for a 3 star property. The lobby is nice and our room on the 9th floor (city view) was in great shape. I think this is the highest floor you can have for city view so definitely request it. It looked as if it had been recently remodeled. The hotel is located a short 3-5 minute walk to the beach was no big deal for my son. It is located near the beach that has the wave breaker, thus you do not need to worry about your little ones getting caught up in the waves. You also pass a the McDonalds on the way to the beach!If you are thinking of taking the public bus known as the The Bus to Hanauma Bay from this hotel, know that people from all the other Waikiki hotels will already have boarded and it will be standing room only for about 35-45 minutes to Hanauma. Tough for a 6 year old. We caught a 10:50 bus so it may have been better if we went earlier.The breakfast buffet was $14.95 for adults, which I thought was a little expensive. We bought cereal and milk from the ABC store for half our breakfasts to save money. There is a small fridge in the room.If you haven't been to Waikiki before, know that you do not have to pack beach towels. This hotel said it was okay to use the pool towels down at the beach. It seemed like most people did this. Overall, the bell boys, housekeeping staff and front desk were very friendly and helpful. I would definitely stay here again.  
<Date>Jun 24, 2005

<Author>Bristolmember
<Content>Good Place to Stay We visited OAHU in March 2005 and enjoyed staying at this hotel. We did intially ask for an upgrade and got put in the club lounge suites on the top floor which was high up! I think it was around floor 38? Although the suite was large and absolutely gorgeous and even had an ajoining room where you could get snacks and drinks, we decided to move as it was just too high up and we were beginning to suffer from vertigo! If you like heights and enjoy vacating in style I would definitely recommend the upgrade to the club lounges as they are good value for money.The room which we 'down graded ' to was nice if a little noisy as we had a connecting door to the room next door. Also the walls/flooring are not too thick there so you could often here flushes being pulled in the surrounding rooms toilets.We ate once in the hotels restaurant and although the food was fine the staff on duty were a bit miserable and it was quite expensive.I was a little disappointed with OAHU, I found that it was too Americanised and did not seem to of retained much of its original culture/features. There were too many fast food joints/restaurants for my liking. I would not recommend travelling around Waikiki at night as it appears to be full of drunken louts and prostitutes. Whilst walking on Kuhio Avenue around 9ish we witnessed a number of violent fights between local residents and drunk american tourists.I would advise people to visit the Polynesian Cultural Centre, the South Shore, Dole Pineapple Centre and Honolulu Zoo when staying in OAHU.If you want to get alway from the hustle and bustle of Waikiki Beach I would recommend a short bus ride to Kahala Beach which is clean and quiet , has stunning views and amenities.Had a good time there but after 18hours of flying I don't think I will be rushing back too soon!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Prince Kuhio is just the best!!! This was our first trip to Hawaii, our 25th anniversary, and the Prince Kuhio could not have been nicer. We loved our room, 31st floor, ocean view, king bed. We thought the room was great. Big enough for the two of us. The fridge was nice to keep bottled water cold, a big TV that we never turned on, an in room safe that we didn't use, coffee in the room, and anything else we needed we just asked. The maid service was excellent. Always neet and clean. I had a $75 meal voucher that came with my room package. When we checked in I asked it we could apply it toward the free continental breakfast. The desk person then gave us both a free breakfast ticket for the entire stay, 8 days, and the breakfast buffet was the BEST! Everything is so close. Kuhio Ave. is a Bus route, beach is a block away, all the big tour buses pick up at the hotel just a half a block away. Fast food is close by, and so are the expensive ones, and it is a little quieter although we couldn't keep the balcony door open all night due to the steet noise. They are working on the other two elevators and that was the only problem during peak times but who's in a hurry when your in Paradise? When we go back we will stay here again, promise! Aloha!

<Author>moxie
<Content>Nice hotel, but small rooms Good pool area with a bar/grill and nice lounge chairs, but no view of the ocean from the pool area--It's VERY windy up on the 10th floor. The hotel is nice and clean and the wait for elevators wasn't bad. The room was very small; however, we got a great deal so it was worth it. I liked that it had a refrigerator in the room. The Radisson upgraded us to a higher floor (no charge) for a better view. We didn't want to pay the $40 extra for ocean view, but the moutain view was nice too. The business center offers convenient and free use of their computers and Internet. It was one long or 3 short blocks walk to the beach, about 5 minutes walk, 10 minutes to the zoo. Go West on Kuhio about 7 blocks to find great dining deals, such as $2.75 breakfast (2 pancakes, 2 eggs, 2 bacon) and seafood dinners for $10. Don't be put off, by the appearance of these places, the food is great. Cheeseburger in Paradise was a little pricey, but great music and a decent view of the ocean and surfers.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Radisson Prince Kuhio Great Stay Just returned from a seven night stay at the Prince Kuhio. We found the hotel to be a great place to stay at an affordable price. It really is only two blocks to the beach! It's an easy walk. On the way to the beach is a McDonalds for a quick breakfast and they serve fresh pineapple every day.The hotel is very clean, newly renovated, and the staff are most accomodating. The rooms are nice, but a bit small. Who spends time in their rooms while in Hawaii, anyway? There is a very large lobby area which is beautifully decorated. The hotel offers what they call Hospitality Rooms for travelers like us whose departure time is after check out time. Our flight did not leave until that night, so after we checked out we spent the day shopping in the city and went back to the hotel and had the hospitality room for an hour to shower, change and relax a few minutes. There is no charge for this and it really added to their already over the top hospitality. I would definitely stay here again. And they give returning guests a discount. The hotel offers parking at $10 a day for self-park. The location is great, everything you need is within walking distance. It is right on the the bus route, so you can take the city bus to places further away.

<Author>ExcitedMom
<Content>Happy we decided to stay at the RPK We stayed at the RPK March 24-April 1 (1 adult and 3 children) and were delighted with our stay. Although the property is rated as a 3 Star using the American Automobile Association standards (with a 4 Star being a fancy hotel and a 5 Star being incredibly rare), it had many features of a 4 Star property including a fabulous lobby, a hairdressing salon, room-service, and a nice restaurant. As described in all previous reviews, the staff were very helpful, including Howard the concierge. They have one of the few heated pools in Honolulu, and keep it open 7AM until midnight. I'd been told the pool was small but was pleasantly surprised to find it was 50 ft long, so could do lengths in it (although it got crowded late afternoon). The hot-tub is a nice tiled one, and was perfect temperature (nice and hot!). Unfortunately, it was very windy every day, so we didn't make as much use of the nice lounge chairs and the pool bar-snack shop as we otherwise would have. One nice bonus is that they allow you to take their towels to the beach, which saved lots of sand from being tracked into our room. We were thrilled to get upgraded to the 28th floor with a mountain view (although lower floors would have saved some long waits for the elevator, and might have made the balcony more useful as it really was too windy to sit out most of the time). The location of the hotel couldn't be better. We walked to the zoo in under 10 minutes (the facilities at the zoo could use some upgrading, but that did not detract from the beautiful animals they have with a great collection of birds and reptiles including the largest tortoises we'd ever seen - all for $6 for adults and $1 for kids). Kuhio Beach was about a 5 minute walk from the hotel, and was preferable to other beaches as the sand was finer, and they had a walled-off area for kids to play. The beach is crowded, but perfect for people-watching. We bought boogie boards for $14 at ABC which was a great investment (and they even survived the flight home). There is an area with shaded and sunny benches right behind the sand on Kuhio Beach which would be perfect for someone who loved the beach but can't get up and down from the sand anymore. They even had muscial groups playing traditional Hawaiian music there some days. A little south of there is the beach where they show free movies every Saturday and Sunday - just take your beachmat. The rooms are not fancy (picture a Best Western or a Holiday Inn with a bit nicer furniture) but they have recently been refurbished, and had marble bathrooms. One or two free newspapers every day was another nice bonus.A few suggestions about things to do:1) Hanuama Bay - Try to get there early as you have to watch a 7-min video about the reef before you can go to the beach, and we waited over an hour to see the video. We wished we had rented a dry snorkel (has an extra valve so less water gets in so good for beginners). It would be a shame to miss Hanauma Bay unless you have no intention of snorkelling.2) Pearl Harbour - We took the city bus (75 min ride but get to see lots of the city) so arrived at 9:30 AM, but again waited in line to get a 1 PM ticket to see the video and ride the boat to the memorial (all of which is free). However, because of the wait, we paid to tour the Bowfin Submarine, which was as interesting as the video and boat ride ($8 for adults). We didn't tour the Missouri battleship ($16 for adults) but would if we went back. One hitch with taking the bus is that we waited at the wrong stop to go back to the hotel, so ask the driver where to wait when he lets you off. However, it appeared that you had to pay at least $9 per person for the van tours to Pearl Harbour and the bus is only $2 ($1 for kids), so I guess it depends what your budget is.3) exercise - I jogged from hotel most mornings. The sidewalks along the canal or the beach were not too crowded, but might have been after 7:30 AM. I didn't rent a bike, but there was a place to rent not far from the zoo, and there were bike trails, but perhaps not as extensive of a trail system as in most American cities these days. People who complain about Waikiki clearly didn't realize they had chosen to go to a big city on a beach. It is not like the quiet romantic resorts you find on the other Hawaiian islands, but offers lots of shopping, restaurants, and entertainment at a much more reasonable price. I would not hesitate to go back and to stay at the RPK again.  
<Date>Apr 5, 2005

<Author>nearandfar2
<Content>Good choice We stayed in the Prince Kuhio for five nights in March 2005. We found it a good choice. The hotel is a long block from the beach, but offered good ocean views because there are no tall buildings between it and the ocean. We recommend the higher floors, just below the concierge level. We were on the 28th floor, which was fine. The rooms were modern, comfortable, and clean. At the eastern end of Waikiki beach, the hotel is a half-mile or so from the main shopping areas. But getting to them was easy enough. A plus is that the hotel is on the street that is the main bus line. We bought the four day tourist pass for $20 and a bus guide (both available right across the street at the convenience store), which we found a bargain. Buses go everywhere, including the major out of town beaches. You can even take a bus that goes all the way around the island for no extra charge. The hotel was accomodating and honored our request for a high floor and early check in. I called the hotel directly to reserve a room, and after a bit of negotiating they threw in a complimentary buffet breakfast each day for each of us. At about $170 a night, it was a good value, especially with the breakfast. There are certainly swankier hotels in town, but on a value for money basis, the Prince Kuhio is hard to beat.  
<Date>Apr 3, 2005

<Author>TS7
<Content>A fortunate find! Giving the Radisson Prince Kuhio 5-stars means that I can't find one thing to complain about! Staff: Really great, totally helpful and friendly. From the bellman to the servers to the maids to the cooks, everyone was a pleasure to deal with.Location: The reason I booked this hotel (last minute) was to balance out the high price of airfare, and a quick check on this site showed glowing reviews for reasonable rates. I'm guessing the rates are slightly lower than others because this hotel is one block from the beach! Literally a 3 minute walk, at most. I'm so glad I didn't insist on a beachfront hotel, which would have cost 1000 more dollars all to save just a 3 minute walk!Recommendation: When you book the room, make sure the contintental breakfast is included! I somehow stumbled into it, (booked through Orbitz), and it's the best choice I made! Different food every morning, banana pancakes, macadamia nut pancakes, breakfast rice (the best food ever), mishu soup, plus all the regular breakfast food. I've never looked forward to breakfast so much, and as I'd already paid for it, it was as simple as stepping off the elevator, handing the server a card, they mark it, and you're eating within moments. Perfection.Summary: With other beachfront hotels, you're paying for the multiple oceanfront pools, with bars, music, etc. Anyone can walk to these and order just the same as a guest, so I was happy to pay less at the Prince Kuhio and walk.
