<Author>Blakeysmom
<Content>Really great vacation! My husband and I just returned from Oahu today and I wanted to write immediately to say that we LOVED the Radisson Prince Kuhio! It was a very clean hotel and the staff was very helpful and seemed as excited to have us there as we were to be there! The rooms were nice and kept very clean. If you are booking a mountain view room-ask for one that ends in 19-you will get a wrap around lanai that overlooks the mountains on one side and the ocean on the other. Our room was 3219 and it was awesome! There is a bus stop a half block away and it is one block to the ocean. I only wish it were one or two blocks closer to the center of Waikiki-we walked about twenty miles in 6 days-no joke! This was our first trip to Hawaii and definitely not our last! Some other great things-whale watching this time of year with Star of Honolulu tours was amazing, we took the circle island tour from E Noa-Captain Rob is the best tour guide ever, we also would recommend attending the swap meet at Aloha Stadium and an airport shuttle transfer from Holoholo tours-it is family owned and they are some of the friendliest people we have ever met-and it is only $6 per way! Hope this helps any of you on the fence about the hotel or any of these services! Aloha

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Radisson Prince Kuhio was FANTASTIC! My husband and I have talked about going to Hawaii, our dream destination, for about 37 years, so when we finally decided to go, I wanted everything to be as perfect as possible. So when I found this website, I was thrilled to have first hand reviews reagarding hotels and even some entertainment tips. I did extensive study and research on this site, and I might say it was confusing sometimes seeing that one person might regard their hotel stay excellent, while another at the same hotel was terrible. But I decided to go with the hotel's ranking number, along with our budget, and made the decision to stay at the Radisson Prince Kuhio. We were there November 22-24. I'll have to say we were thoroughly satisfied. The staff was extremely friendly, our bellboy was so nice and also gave us some ideas for eating out. The remodeling was all complete and the lobby is absolutely gorgeous. We had reserved an oceanview room, and when we arrived, we asked to be as high as possible and was put on the 33rd floor. We also asked to be away from the elevators, as I had read from other reviews that they can be quite noisy. We were about 5 rooms away, and never heard a peep! Our room was great, very spacious, and the view was just beautiful. There were no other buildings to block our views at all, especially that high. The balcony was a bit tiny, but at that height, we didn't spend much time out there anyway. We only stayed two nights, before we boarded our cruise ship, but we found that even the hustling and bustling Waikiki was a great experience. We also highly recommend the Polynesian Cultural Center.(be sure and take some rain gear for the unexpected showers)Even though the lua food wasn't that tasty, the center itself, and the Horizons night show was unbelievable. If you have some extra time, rent a car and go to the north shore, to a town called Kaliewa. You can watch surfers all up and down the shore. And about a mile or two out of town, is the Audobon Society Preserve. Even if you don't pay to go in, you can drive through some of the grounds and it is just beautiful. It was fantastic. So all in all, our entire trip to Hawaii was the dream come true we had waited for and would stay at the Radisson Prince Kuhio again, in a heartbeat.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>ok, but could have been better! We just got back from Hawaii on January 1st. The Radisson recently completed renovations in the lobby area but they have many floor tiles scheduled to be changed. The pool area also completed renovations but from the look of it I could not tell anything had been done. I would have liked to see the Radisson before the renovations???? The rooms were ok but a little small. The elevators were slow most of the time especially if you were on the 10th floor (Pool Deck) trying to go up. The breakfast buffet was ok too. The menu for the most part was the same each day so it got old after 5 days. If you are looking for surf lessons then stop by to see Roger Brown. He is located by the Duke Staue on Waikiki beach across from the Hyatt. He only charges $25.00/hour per person unlike the $100+ that other surfing companies charge. He is the best.The polynesian culture center was awesome. The Luau show was the best I have gone to and I have been to Hawaii 3 times and to 3 luau's. You will not be disappointed.The food in Waikiki is the best and has many places to choose from. I liked the Cheesecake factory the best but it can be a little pricey if you are on a budget. The cheeseburger in Paradise was great too.Overall the Radisson is just ok and very average. If this is what you are looking for in a hotel then this is for you. If you want a better hotel for the same price then look some where else.Mahalo

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Enjoyed our stay, BUT This hotel is located one block back from the hustle and bustle of Kalakaua Ave (main strip in Waikiki). The hotel is a little dated, but more than adequate for a comfortable stay.The pool is not huge, but is located on the roof top of the car park on level 10 which is far enough away from rooms to avoid unnecessary noise.However, the plumbing within the hotel seemed a little noisy. We could hear people washing their hands, having a shower and flushing their toilet as if they were in our bathroom.There is a business centre on the ground floor which provides free internet access which is handy. The staff at the front desk and the concierge were always helpful and friendly.Lu Au - don't go to Germaine's Lu Au. Do yourself a favour and save $US 47.50 per person. Imagine an army camp style kitchen, long queues, cardboard trays for plates, slop for food. The Lu Au was supposed to be on a secluded beach. Unfortunately, the Lu Au was held on a mock beach at the back of an industrial park with dirt for sand. The hosts were annoying, the food was very average.Don't expect an intimate Lu Au. THe one we were on had a mere 900 people.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Relaxed stay at the Radisson Just spent a week in Waikiki, Honolulu and my stay at the Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio really helped me enjoy myself.Great location, at the quieter end of Waikiki. Beach is only a couple of minutes walk away and staff at the pool will happily give you towels to take down there.Had an ocean view and definitely worth it, though the view of the mountains behind is nice too. The staff in there were particularly friendly and helpful - real pleasure to have breakfast.Likewise the staff at the desk were helpful in dealing with my request for a late check out.All in all a clean, friendly hotel well worth staying in. I would definitely look at staying there again on a return trip.

<Author>Bevzvet
<Content>Wonderful visit at the Radisson Prince Kuhio This is a wonderful place to stay in Waikiki. Our room, which was booked over the internet, was $129.00 and when we arrived we upgraded to an oceanfront room for an extra $40. It was worth it. We ended up getting a corner room giving, us a view of the ocean and Diamond head. The room was spotlessly cleaned daily and though the bathroom was little small it had a nice sized tub. The view was spectacular from our balcony. The service we received was outstanding and special mention must go to Howard at the concierge's desk who helped us book our trips and tours. He greeted us daily with a smile on his face and his offer to help us in anyway he could He suggested severals tours that were much better (and cheaper) than the ones we have picked out. The Discover Hawai'i Circle Island tour with Cousin Rolland as your guide was the absolute best. Security was not an issue. We felt safe and there is also a safe in your room for which you are charged a daily rate of $3.00 but only if you use it. I would not recommend the Waikiki Trolley. It was $25.00 per day per person. The routes change twice a year, but this was not publisized. We spent the first four hours trying to get to one place because they kept putting us on different trolleys to transfer us to our destination. It would have been easier to take the bus.

Great service!The walk to the beach isn't bad, it's only a few small blocks to walk. <Author>marshabell
<Content>Wonderful experience, a beautiful hotel for the money!!! We stayed at the Prince Kuhio from 10/23-11/2. we got an excellent deal from priceline and really did not know what to expect. i made sure to read the reviews on here before i left and have to admit i was a bit skeptical, but we paid less than $70 a night, so i was willing to put up with just about anything. First of all, the elevators were incrediby fast. the hotel has over 35 floors so it has to be. the toilets are loud, but honestly, unless you eat some bad sushi, how many times do you actually have to flush the toilet in the course of your day?? we stayed on the 3rd floor and kuhio street is VERY noisy and we could hear it all. This was not really a problem since the construction stops at 5pm and we were always up nice and early since we were operating on mainland time. if it really bothers you, ask for a room above the 7th or 8th floor. The pool on the 10th floor was beautiful, and never crowded. the pool bar had good drink deals. The lobby is beautiful and very impressive. it's nice that it is the first impression you get of the hotel, because they have obviously put a lot of time and money into it. Housekeeping was excellent and we were never without anything. There's an ABC store across the street and we visited it on a daily basis. get your film developed there before you leave, it's cheaper and you don't have to worry about the airport xray ruining it. we ate breakfast a few times in the trellises restaurant, very good food, but the buffet was $15 for breakfast which is a bit much, so we walked a few blocks to keoni's for their $4.99 deal. it's a great place for dinner too, a thai/american joint, a local's favorite. the hotel staff was very nice and very funny. they answered any questions with a smile and were very eager to help. please consider the radisson prince kuhio for your stay. you will not be dissappointed. it is one block from the beach and an excellent value. This was our second trip to waikiki within a year and we stayed at the ohana waikik malia last time. This was ten thousand times better! hope this was helpful!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A great time! We stayed at the Radisson 10/12-10/19 and our stay was outstanding. I had researched the Radisson for a long time so I was aware of what to expect. When we walked into the lobby they were just giving it the finishing touches and it was emaculate! We were greeted by a friendly receptionist who I believe her name was Frills. When we checked in we were immediatly up-graded to an ocean-view room on the eleventh floor. ( Not bad for a Priceline customer) We were given a room on the opposite end from the elevators so that meant our balcony was bigger than most because it went around the corner of the building. The view was spectacular! Every mornng and evening we would sit out there and enjoy the scenery and fresh breeze. For those who complained about the noise, of course there is noise you are in a city---a busy city! There were five elevators and most of the time within 20-30 seconds we were in the elevator. Our housekeeper was very friendly and polite. On our second day when I saw him I asked for an extra coffee pouch of the regular coffee instead of the decaffinated. Every day he made sure I had two pouches of the regular. Later in the week he saw me going into the room and gave me a handful of pouches. My wife is a clean-freak and she was delighted to stay at this hotel. We never saw one bug--there was no sand in the bed--------and everything was clean and sparkling! Everyone was friendly, even the guys in the garage. Even the bell- men we met in the elevator made conversation and gave us help as to where to eat. For those few who found the Radisson employees rude, I have found that usually you receive what you give out. Give friendliness and you get friendliness. No one, including people whose occupation means serving others needs will go the extra mile for customers who are rude and mean spirited. The Hotel is a block from the beach ( About 3 minutes) but I realized this was good thing because it was away from all the busyness of the main strip. The Hotel (because it is away from most of the heavy foot traffic) caters to those of us who want to get away from all the excitement when it's time to go to the room and relax and tone down. I felt secure and safe the whole time I spent at the Radisson. I would definitely stay at the Radisson again.

<Content>Another wonderful stay at the Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio My best friend and I booked a seven night stay at the Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio during the last week of June 2004. This was our second stay at the hotel. We booked the trip through Pleasant Holidays on the internet. We chose a double mountain room which included the buffet each morning. We checked in at almost 11:00 PM, and we were upgraded to a ocean view room on the 22nd floor. The room was very clean, and the view was so beautiful that we never closed the curtains throughout our entire stay. The buffet was an excellent way to start each day. We have decided never to book a hotel room that does not include this option. The staff was very friendly and helpful. The Pool area really looks nice, and is kept very clean. We rented a car for our entire stay so we spent most of each day beach hopping on the island. It was awesome coming home to a beautifu clean room each afternoon. At night we met up with old friends and had a couple of great dinners at the Cheesecake Factory. It was great to be able to walk around without being hassled. The street below the hotel was being torn up and the lobby was being remodeled during our stay, but noise was not an issue as we were gone most of the day. The zoo was an easy walk from the hotel and we took advantage of the free Wednesday night concert. What a nice evening that was. The Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio is definitly our first choice when staying in the city. We will be back !!

<Author>mkayme
<Content>A great hotel My husband and I stayed here for 5 days in early September 2004. We chose this hotel because it is in the quieter end of Waikiki Beach. Although this hotel was on a very busy street, you would have never known that while inside. The beach is within easy walking distance, only one block away. We stayed on the 15th floor and had a great view of the ocean. We were upgraded from a mountain view to an ocean view at no charge. Our package included a breakfast buffet, which was well worth it. The buffet had a variety of choices that varied from day to day. They also had dinner specials daily for about $10.00 an entre. The food was very good and the service was excellent. The general atmosphere of the hotel was quiet and we saw very few children. Our floor was also very quiet and I rarely ever heard any noise in the hallway. We arranged all our tours through the hotel and we were very satisfied. If you are looking for a quiet, affordable, 3 1/2 - 4 star hotel than this is the place for you. It was under renovations while we were there, but nothing that interfered with our vacation. The pool area is completed, the lobby was almost done, and I believe the restaurant and bar area are next. The staff were very friendly and I would definitly stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Our Place to Stay in Paradise We had the pleasure of staying at the Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio from September 17 to September 22, 2004. We had booked a vacation package on Priceline, which included a standard room, below the 10th floor. We were given the option of upgrading to a room with a view on a higher floor for an additional $40 per night, but opted to go with the standard room.The standard room came with 2 double beds, coffee, hairdryer, iron and ironing board, and a safe was available for an additional charge. The room was neat, and impecably clean. The room was located in the back of the hotel overlooking the courtyard and the coy pond. We had a beautiful view of the mountains, and from our balcony saw a rainbow everyday.The maid and staff were very courteous, and even addressed us by name. The cleaning staff did an excellent job of keeping our room clean, and every morning, we received a fresh local newspaper at our door.The pool area was also neat and clean, and fresh towels were provided to hotel guests. However. we were not impressed with the bar in the pool area, or with the worker there. There was a sports game on TV, and the bartender was more interested in the game than serving his customers. We literally had to ask 3 times for service, and when we did receive our drinks, they were substandard and extremely overpriced ($32.00 for 4 drinks, not including tip)I would like to say the Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio was a wonderful place to stay. We were very comfortable in our room, air condition, hot water and water pressure were great, and we were far enough away from the beach so that the noise was not bothersome at all, even though the beach was only about a 3 minute walk from the hotel. Noise from other rooms or guests was never an issue, and there was never a wait for an elevator.We'll be returning to Oahu in the spring, and we look forward to our next stay at the Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio

<Content>Excellent! Excellent! Just got back from a stay here from 9/14-9/21. My sister and I visited Waikiki for the first time and upon arriving in Honolulu - we were ready to go home -- Until we arrived at the Raddisson. From the front desk (Paul), to housekeeping, to the valet service - it was a fabulous service. We got a terrific deal on Priceline so we were expecting to be short - shifted as usually happans when booking through them. However, we showed up early and they had a room ready on the fifth floor with a partial ocean view that was fabulous. There was construction that was going on in the hotel but never bothersome or intrusive. As for the noise on the road (KUHIO), to all the other reviewers -- GET OVER IT!!! It is part of the price you pay for staying in Waikiki. How do you think a commercialized, tourist zone gets their trash taken away, or food delivered? I was able to sleep just fine, even through the noise and deliveries. The best part of this hotel is it's location. It's at the end of hotel row and a 2 minute walk to the beach. Or if you like, do what we did and discover non-tourist beaches that are a short 20 minute drive away!! Whatever you decide, do choose the Radisson. It was well worth it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Radisson - Would definitely Stay Again After exhaustive research, we booked the Radisson from 9/1-9/6. We liked it so much we came back for our last night in Waikiki. We booked through the Hawaii Visitors Bureau and originally had a ridge view room w/breakfast. Immediately switched to ocean view for 20.00/night and we thought worth it. Our last night was on the Kuhio floor and again, worth every penny. Only drawback was a bit of water damage on ceiling which I thought could easily be fixed to make the room Perfect! The lobby renovation is set to be completed 9/24 and while a bit annoying it was so minimal I can't believe others mentioned it (unless you are planning on sleeping or staying in the lobby - it was no bother). Once, on Sat. we waited about 1 minute for an elevator and occassionally it was a bit backed up but really - NO BIG DEAL. Everyone was very friendly and helpful. We loved that the staff (Janet-front desk, Linda and I think Rene in restaurant) and a lot of others remembered us by name. We give high marks for the room, the service, the location is the BEST and will always stay here when in Waikiki. The beach is less than 3 min walk and it's the best in Waikiki - a beautiful, uncrowded, shady park is at the end of the street and a nice swimming area. The other hotels (more expensive) didn't have nice beaches or were so crowded you had to sit on top of your neighbor. We ate at a Korean bbq next door (yokitini sp?) that was terrific. The hotel breakfast kept us full until dinner and was varied/good every day. Just can't say enough good. We also read and asked about the lounge on our last day and were given keys to a hospitality suite for 1 hour - we showered and enjoyed this amenity. Didn't use the internet - walked to Ocean Resort and paid 1.00 to use theirs. VERY HAPPY - You will not be dissapointed - very clean, well kept, hotel. You can not beat the location. Also, liked the mai tais at Mai tai bar in the pink hotel - sit in 'toys' section (not the right spelling but excellent waitress - also remembered us from 1 week ago). Buy cheap bamboo beach mat from ABC and sit in shade at kuhio beach - no need to rent expensive umbrellas. Bring snacks but buy all else at cheap abc stores. We brought beach chairs and umbrellas and snorkel sets (also can be bought cheaply at abc stores) that we wouldn't bring again. (too much weight). Sorry so long but hope this is helpful.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The higher the room the better, at this hotel. As the final leg of our 4-island 15-day 25th wedding anniversary trip, we booked a 4-night stay in an ocean view king room at the Radisson Hotel on Waikiki Beach for August 3-7. 2004. We had just come from Poipu Beach on Kauai and due to an early flight we were confirmed for early check-in, which went off without any problems. The hotel is located at the far, east end (toward Diamond Head) and 2 city blocks off the beach. It an older hotel but the main floor was in the process of being renovated and will probably be real nice when completed. Its location from this end and the beach makes it easier to navigate in, out of and around traffic. Upon check-in they told us we were on the 27th floor right next to their main (only) elevator bank and asked if this would be a problem. Because we are both light sleepers they gave us another room 2-doors off the elevator on the 20th floor, and with 2 double beds rather than a king. Even though it was nice that they immediately informed us about our room location, I felt extremely disappointed and couldn understand why we had been assigned such an unpleasant room in the first place especially given the fact we had booked our accommodations 10 months out. As for our new room, it was updated, very clean and nicely decorated although the bathroom is a bit on the small side. It's location to the street made it a pretty noisy room with lots of city traffic and people noise. The room also has a small crescent shaped balcony with 2 chairs and a small table. Because there is another hotel located 1 block down, across from the beach, the ocean view from this floor was just okay and would have been a lot better from the 27th floor or higher, and would have also been much quieter, as Kuhio Avenue is very busy and noisy. We also rented a car and therefore had to pay $7 per night for hotel parking located in their multi-level parking garage that had convenient, secure access into the hotel. The hotel pool and hot tub are located on the rooftop above the garage and has secure access from the hotel 10th floor. There are guest towels and a bar located next to the pool with plenty of places to sit and relax. Our room rate also included a breakfast buffet that was served in their main restaurant (Trellisses) located on the 1st floor. There is a lovely garden located just outside the restaurant windows and they offered a nice variety of items every morning that made our dining experience very enjoyable. As for foot access to the beach, mall and downtown areas, it was very easy. Within 10 minutes you can walk to many of the beach attractions and restaurants including the international market, and there are loads of city and trolly buses that will take you just about anywhere you want to go. Overall, our experience at the Radisson was pleasant and would have been much better save for the initial room assignment. On our next trip, we'll probably try the Marriott Waikiki, located just to the east of the Radisson and across from the beach. We we visited their facility and on our last night, had a wonderful seafood buffet at their restaurant.  
<Date>Sep 7, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Radisson Waikiki is Great Value! We just returned from a wonderful trip to Waikiki on August 29. The Radisson Waikiki Prince Kuhio (NOT to be confused with the Waikiki Prince - that is a different hotel) was a great choice. We booked our trip through Expedia, and an ocean view room with full breakfast every day was $150 a night. The pool, as mentioned in other reviews, was small, but very adequate. The poolside bar has a limited menu, but great bargains throughout the day (pitcher of beer for $6 from 1-4, pitcher of Mai-Tai's for $8 from 4-7, etc). The only problem we encountered was that the first two nights were VERY noisy from the elevator. The first night we got in very late and were tired and it didn't really bother us. The second night it was EXTREMELY noisy, and we realized that, while the street was noisy (we could hear it from the 24th floor) the elevators were the bulk of the noise we were hearing. We requested a different room, and were given another ocean view room with an even larger lanai (balcony) and absolutely quiet. All employees from the hostess/waitressess in the restaurant to the desk clerks, maids and bellmen were VERY friendly and helpful. I thought the rooms were a bit small, but very nice - don't know why previous reviewers thought the rooms outdated, ours seemed modern enough. And our room was VERY clean - certainly no evidence of bugs as mentioned in an earlier review.Parking was $9 a night, but if you don't get a rental car, you can take the bus almost anywhere, and the beach is an easy 5-10 minute walk.All in all, we had a wonderful time at the Radisson.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>OK....just Stayed here between the 12-24th August 2004. Got an ocean view room on the 24th floor and saw no evidence of any bugs that an earlier reviewer mentioned. The bathroom is quite small (about 7 foot square) but was perfectly adequate. No problem with the water pressure or hot water as reported by other reviewers. The staff were very friendly and helpful, especially the maid staff. The air conditioning worked perfectly well and is adjustable via a control panel near the sink. It automatically turns off when the patio door is opened. Sound insulation between the rooms was generally very good... except for the toilet which i will mention later......Now the bad bits. Was forced to make an international call home from the bedroom phone in the middle of the night. 10 minutes cost........$89.......This is not a misprint........If you need to make an international call, go to the ABC store over the road and buy a $10 phone card and use it in the pay phones near to the lifts (elevators). This phone card gave me one and a half hours of calls to the UK for the $10. The use of the room safe costs $3 per day + tax which in some hotels would be free. Breakfasts were excellent and a slightly different variety every day. However... there were three of us and so i had to pay for the third breakfast buffet ...$15 per day unless you got down there between 6-7am, then it was $10, although in fairness there were cheaper options then to go for the buffet. The drinks in the pool bar tasted like they were watered down and were not good value. However, the most annoying problem were the toilets that were horrendously noisy. So much so that you could hear all the surrounding rooms. Kuhio Ave is noisy and the second busiest road in Waikiki and i could imagine that on the lower floors noise might be a problem. The renevations in the reception area were not a problem and it should look nice when it is finished. I am not a great traveller and do not regularly use hotels and so this must be considered when reading this review. Generally the question is would i stay here again and the answer is yes. It is based only about 150 yds from Kuhio beach and is in the quieter part of an otherwise very busy part of Waikiki. The staff were friendly whilst not being intrusive and the rooms were clean and tidy with only some minor signs of wear and tear. The pool looked well maintained and clean. The down sides were the cost of calls, noisy toilets and the cost of additional breakfasts.

But it's Hawaii and fortunately you don't spend much time in a hotel room so I had a wonderful vacation anyway. Oh and I would definitely recommend skydiving while in Hawaii. <Content>Great Location  I stayed at the Radisson in Waikiki for 7 nights and it was exceptional, far exceeding what I expected for the price I paid (I purchased an air+hotel package from Priceline and the total bill was ~1400 round-trip from Kansas City). It is along the much quieter strip (Kuhio) than the more glamorous strip one block away which was perfect, especially if you're the type that wants peace but to still be steps away from all the action, too. Great Location! The staff was extremely helpful and the grounds were very clean. We had a view of the lush, tropical gardens below and the landscaping was gorgeous. The only complaint I would have is that I had requested a room with one large bed but upon arrival was given a room with two full size beds, instead. It was a slight inconvenience, but nothing that I wasn't willing to overlook. Overall a wonderful experience and I would definitely return!

The area: Good location and the low buildings out front made the view good for all tut the very lowest floors on the ocean side. The beach right out front is nice because there is a breakwater built that keeps out all the big waves, surfers and boogie boarders. Il defiantly be back.

<Content>Great Hotel We stayed at the Radisson May 22-30, 2004 and at that time the hotel was still under construction. Pool access still consisted of using a nearby hotel's pools and hot tubs. <Content>Awesome hotel=) After reading reviews on tripadvisor, we decided to go with this hotel because it was said to be decent for the inexpensive price. I booked us a 7 night package which included airfare from SFO on priceline. As i've read before, priceline guests have the lower rooms. Not necessarily true. When we arrived to our room, we had a spectacular ocean view on the 28th floor. The balconies were very calming with the warm weather, watching the surfers. One night we even watched fireworks go off over the water right in front of our hotel! The housekeeping staff excellent and friendly as well. The elevators are extremely fast. I had read before (and was also told by a friend) that the elevators at the radisson prince kuhio are VERY SLOW. thats not true at all! They gave us the newspaper every day, which included a brief bulletin for the day of whats going on at the hotel. The rooms were big with a nice tropical/contemporary decor. The front desk guy (RON) even warmed up my boyfriends prime rib left overs in the staff microwave at 2am! thats how nice they are here =) The only down sides of the hotel would be the fact that the room service food sucks. =P And the water pressure of the showerhead was not strong enough. All the construction on kuhio was a little annoying too, but as far as the construction in the hotel, we didnt mind it because you cant hear it from the rooms. AWESOME HOTEL. i'd definitely stay here again. We had a really good price. I recommend going to ONO. Its a restaurant off kapahulu. They serve the BEST local hawaiian food. And if ur into Thai food, make sure to go to SINGHA'S THAI CUISINE. It's exquisite. Although, we didnt get to go this time around, i went the last time i was in hawaii and i recommend it!

<Author>deadlinemom
<Content>Location, value, service - we'll be back! My family of four stayed here June 19-24. We give it a hearty eight thumbs up! We were hoping for a room at the 20th floor or above, but the busy summer season had begun and our check-in clerk could only offer the 9th floor. We accepted it reluctantly, having been scared off by earlier reviewers' tales of noise and poor views. But we had no problem at all. Our city view room (903) included a stunning sweep of emerald mountains and swaying palms beyond the hotel towers. We were awakened each morning by the creep of salmon-colored sky over those mountains. Best of all, we had easy access to the pool and bar on the 10th floor. My husband and I enjoyed going there for a mini-pitcher of Mai-Tais each day at 4 p.m As everyone has remarked, the staff is wonderful--friendly and full of good advice. The hotel is centrally located in Waikiki, with beach less than 5 minute walk away. If you'll be there over a weekend, take advantage of free movies on Prince Kuhio Beach. And every night, the city provides hula entertainment along the beach promenade. Waikiki's beaches are kid-friendly but we found the waters full of lotion and people. Try some of the more isolated locales on the north and eastern shores. Also, don't miss snorkeling at Hanema Bay! Our adolescent daughters said it was one of the highlights of their trip. The biggest drawback for us was the horrible traffic whenever we ventured out in our car. Be prepared for Hawaii Time: ``15 minutes and however long it takes to get there.'' Lots of renovation continuing in the hotel lobby and exterior, but not a terrible challenge. All in all, a great hotel at a great value.  
<Date>Jun 28, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic Waikiki hotel choice I just returned from a fantastic Hawaii holiday touring Oahu; 3 nights at the Radisson, The Big Island; 5 nights at the Hilton, and 6 nights on Kauai at the Princeville. I went with my partner, both in our late 20s.We found the Radisson to be an excellent choice while in Waikiki:Pluses:It is at the quieter end of Waikiki near Kuhio Beach Park and Kapiolani Park (stunning sunset views)- a big plus for us anyway!Short wait and very friendly check in staffEfficient valet parkingFantastic views (were on 35th floor)Very bright, clean and contemporary decor in the bedroom.Bathroom - bight marble (a bit dated), smaller than average but clean and powerful shower.Beds large and comfortableThe Kuhio club levels don't offer anything more in the rooms but access to the small but very friendly lounge was really good - very nice continental breakfast in the morning, and a seletcion of appetisors in the evening. If you can get these levels at a good rate then go for it but would not pay more than $20 extra.Another big plus is that the price at the Radisson is way below other comparable hotels, and although it does not have all the facilities of say the Hilton, for less money you will get a nice clean room, friendly efficient service and a good start to Hawaii.Negatives:Lobby is under big refurb (but not a big problem)Small but clean pool area (we did not use)Construction on the road outside the hotel can make access at times slow and frustratingLower floors probably offer limited view due to surrounding cityscape and would be quite noisy from traffic etc.It is on Oahu, which was our least favourite island, in terms of touring, but if you like the big city, party atmosphere of Waikiki then thats not a problem either.For info on the Hilton, Big island, and the Princeville read under those reviews.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Friendly, clean, good price My teenage daughter, her friend, and I stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio during Easter week (early April.) We had a great room on the 28th floor with the mountain view. The room was clean and an acceptable size for the three of us. The 5-minute walk to the beach was never a problem. We walked around Waikiki every night to take in the street entertainment, too. The girls ate breakfast at the buffet every morning, since breakfast for two was included in our rate. The buffet offered a wide selection of good food, but I think they got tired of it by mid-week. Next time, I think we'll pass on the breakfast buffet add-on so we could try breakfasts at other places as well. The desk staff was very friendly, and helpful, answering questions cheerfully. I felt that they valued our presence and they genuinely wanted to help us have the best time possible. The maids were very friendly and thorough. I walked into our room while the maid was cleaning and she was very polite and friendly, but made sure that I produced a key for the room to prove that I was not there to 'lift' anything. I appreciated that she was protecting our property, yet handled the situation professionally and courteously. The bellboys held our luggage behind their desk all day on our departure day, since we had an evening flight out. We were able to spend the day at the beach, come back to a special guest room to shower, and leave for the airport fresh and ready for the long trip home. We loved Honolulu and are glad we decided to stay at the Radisson Prince Kuhio. I hope to go back with my husband within a few years, and we will definitely stay there.

<Author>chiguy50
<Content>An Excellent Choice in Waikiki We stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio Waikiki from June 2 to June 8 and found most of the laudatory comments from previous reviewers justified. We booked on Hotwire.com, paying $73 a night for a city-view double. When we got to the hotel, we were allowed to upgrade to a non-smoking king room on the 30th floor with a mountain view for an extra $10 a night. While not a luxury hotel by any standard, the Radisson was well worth the price we paid. Our room was clean and amply furnished, the view was spectacular, and the staff was friendly and helpful. The pool renovations have been completed, but the lobby is still a work in progress. The road construction on Kuhio Ave. was somewhat bothersome from a traffic standpoint but was not a major hassle. We took advantage of the $9.95 early bird breakfast buffet (between 6:00 and 7:00) on several occasions and loved it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Stay there if you can. I was assigned this hotel by Priceline at a very good price.We arrived at about 1:30 on Thursday the 27th. I had arranged for a balloon delivery for my son who would celebrate his 9th birthday while we were in Hawaii. They had it waiting when we arrived and refused a small gratuity for the extra effort.There was no line at the front desk and the gal that assisted us, Janet, was very friendly and helpful. They had us booked on the 7th or 8th floor which was a smoking floor with two double beds. I asked about getting a non-smoking king room and she stated that we could do that, but the room might not be clean yet. I asked about the cost to upgrade to one of their Parlor Suites. She said that this would be $100 extra per night. She then said that we could get a non-smoking king on a high floor with an ocean view for $20 more per night. I don't mind paying a little extra to upgrade to something nice because I usually pay so little with Priceline. This upgrade was worth every penny. The room was not quite ready so we went down the street to have lunch and it was ready when we returned.The room was on the 30th floor with a great view. It was nice to be able to look out and see the boats, surfers and swimmers. We all enjoyed sitting on the Lanai when we were in the room. The room was in great shape and very clean. They were able to remove the sand everyday when they cleaned. The bathtub drained a little slow, but I guess it is nearly impossible to keep up with all the sand that goes down the drain. The room had a safe for $3 per day and a complimentary refrigerator. They had Wayport high speed internet for $9.95 per day. I had purchased a prepaid connection before we left from home which made the price closer to $6 per day. I was also able to get a WiFi signal from the Marriott across the street in my room. The price appeared to be about the same as Wayport.The king sized bed was comfortable and they provided a couple of extra pillows. We brought an air mattress for the kids to sleep on and there was plenty of room for it after I moved the table to the other side of the room. Parking was $9 for self and $12 for valet. We chose the valet for no particular reason. Everytime we wanted the car I phoned down and gave them my ticket number. It was always there waiting when we arrived. We ate two meals at the restaurant. Both were breakfast and both were very good. They had a breakfast special each morning. It included 2 eggs, 2 pancakes and two pieces of bacon for $4.95. They also had a breakfast buffet with a nice variety of food for $14.95. However, if you went between 6 and 7 it was only $9.95. We ate one morning at McDonald's and the breakfast for 4 was just under $30.The walk to the beach was about 6 minutes from our room. They provide complimentary towels to take to the beach. The room was very quiet and we never heard noise from our neighbors or people in the hallway. The elevators were fast and we never had to wait more than about 30 seconds. The pool renovations were finished and the pool opened the day before we left. We walked out there and it appeared to look like just about every other pool we saw while we were there. I printed out a map and directions from mapsonus.com from the airport. The route avoided alot of Waikiki traffic and most of the construction on Kuhio. We had no problems getting in and out of the driveway area. It was a great stay. The whole family discussed it and agreed that there was not one thing we could complain about. Little annoyances have a way of disrupting an entire trip. There were none and the Radisson. We would stay here again and be happy about it. Of course, one of the joys of Priceline is the ability to check out many different places without breaking the bank.

<Author>tgw
<Content>Wonderful Place!! This is one of Honolulu's finest hotels in a great location. Very elegant, yet relaxed. Rooms are nicely decorated and neatly appointed. Like a previous reviewer said, people who book their reservations on Priceline, Hotwire, etc. shouldn't expect the best rooms. I have worked in an upscale hotel, and guests that don't book through the hotel, its central reservations/website, or a travel agent are at the bottom of the totem pole. And rightfully so. The more you pay, the more you get. And just a note... Radisson now has an online best rate guarantee so their rates are now lower than all of those other websites anyway. This hotel offers a nice location for either the beach or the city and the staff is extremely helpful in getting you in the right direction. I have now stayed at this hotel and the Sheraton, and while they are both comparable in physical qualities, price, etc., the staff at the Radisson were awesome and because of that I will return!

<Content>Nice stay overall Just returned from the Radisson and overall, it was a very pleasant experience. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Only a 3 Star This hotel only gets 3 stars from me and shouldnt receive any better. I mostly stay at either Hilton brand hotels or Hyatt hotels and rarely venture to other brands but I decided to try the Radisson. In a world where Radisson is trying to step up to the porch with other finer hotels they fall far short of the top step. The room was clean, but for one of the bed spreads to have some sort of gook on it, but room service changed it after I left a note for them. The room was also nicely decorated Hawaii style while not being tacky about it. If you want an ocean view room you will be staying at the wrong hotel, you will have to share the view with obstruction of other hotels, note the hotel is not beach front as the pictures would have you to believe. Mountain view rooms would be great at this hotel with little to no obstructing views. Thos two should only concern you if you are a person who must have a view of something, but why come to Hawaii and spend considerable time staring out of your window? Yes the pool was closed due to construction, but we did not fly over 10 hrs to spend time at the pool. If you have to use the pool, two other hotels are in conjunction with the Radisson for your use. The remodeling construction was going on in the lobby but looked to soon be completed. Though keep in mind not only is the Radisson going under construction, the whole street of Kuhio is under construction, which is in front of the hotel. Hawaiin's to me look like they dont like to work much, the construction in the hotel and on the streets were only during the hrs of 8-3, at this rate they will never finish. The major draw back to the hotel is the staff, I have stayed at many of hotels and this staffing was not great at all. They had no spirit to them at all, so you never got the feeling of feeling very welcome. You get the since that you are just another revolving customer and not a potential returning customer. We had a late flight leaving home, so of course I needed a late checkout, I called a few days before to ask and I was rudely told not nicely that I need to call back the day I check out and the phone was abruptly hung up. ??? So I called the day I was to check out and they said they would have to see if my room was going to be taken by somebody else, and it was so they gave me a complimentary room for an hour before I left, which was a pain. Instead of doing what any other hotel would normally do, which would swithch those new arrivals to another room in order to accomodate the current customers, remembering you want them to return to your hotel, the hotel was not full and had plenty of room space top make this sort of switch. Parking was fine $9 a day and elevators were very quick, little waiting time for them. The hotel is in a great area of Waikiki, probably the best for the beach (the beach is actually Kuhio beach and not Waikiki), b/c you have a park right there for very open and less crowed beaches. Though the hotels location is not that great, keep in mind that the hotel is not beach front it is a good long block from the beach, and yes I did know this before I booked, though the pictures are very deceptive. If you are looking for a hotel with little to complain about, no roach palace and its location is in a great area, this place is for you, but keep in mind the things I said. Now for Oahu, the island is beautiful, dont get stuck and that tourist trap of Honolulu, rent a car discover the island and hang out at the different beaches, only to go back to Honolulu at night. Beware of crime in the city (Waikiki), especially Kuhio street (not the only street in which this takes place but the roughest I witnessed, it also happens on the boulevard that follows the beach) at night they come crawling out. We were followed one night, untli I just had to stop b/c glances to let the thug know that I knew what he was up to was no good wasnt good enough, so I had to stop my wife and I turned around and just gave him a look, that he needed to make a choice, well he seen I knew then and completely turned around went back wherever he came from, we witnessed this not only with ourselves but from watching other people in the distance. The thugs were sadly to say mostly white trash males and who walked around suspiciously with their hands behind their back (a sure sign). Also on a side street between Kuhio and the boulevard by the beach they had a few prostitutes hanging out at night. Though the hotel is located away from much of this, but this action is only a block from it. Would I go back to Oahu, yes. Would I stay again at the Radisson, more likely not.

<Content>Good hotel We just returned from Oahu last night and had a FABULOUS time! We stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio based on the reviews we read online. <Content>A nice value in the Waikiki area. We stayed here for two nights immediately after our arrival in Apr 2004. We had booked for a Mountain View room and were given a room on the 12th floor. We had booked to stay at the Waikiki Marriott for the remaining five days prior to our arrival itself. We found that to be a far better hotel with bigger rooms and closer to the beach (but more expensive).

<Author>zeuz
<Content>'Luxe Hotel, Ideal Locatin Returning from Hawaii late last night, I'm excited to share my experiences with this hotel with other travelers. This is a quality hotel with great staff waiting to serve your every need and do it in an Aloha way. The vast majority of rooms have fabulous, panoramic views of either Waikiki stretching from Diamond Head to Pearl Harbor or of mountains soaring into the clouds. I really enjoyed watching the rooftop shows from the neighboring Marriott and listening to the music from the nightly beachside hula show from our room. The rooms are large and tastefully decorated with a Hawaiian motif that is not tacky. Elevators are swift and the restaurant overlooking a tropical courtyard is excellent. (We especially enjoyed the weekend buffets allowing us to sample a wide variety of delacies.) While the pool is being renovated, guests have access to either of two luxury hotels across the street. Also, the renovation work in no way impacts guests other than the van from the airport having to use a secondary entrance. We noticed no noise and really no construction activity.The hotel's location is ideal as well. Being on the Diamond Head side of Waikiki allows direct access to the beach a block away as opposed to the limited access of mid-Waikiki hotels. The beach here is especially pretty being open and having a large grassy area as well as a sandy beach. At night, torches glow along the water front. We found this area much less crowded, overly commercial and tacky than those just blocks away. Other hotels nearby include the Hyatt, Marriott and Outrigger, all of which offer shopping of every type as well as additional restaurant choices. One additonal point. The city's public transit system is called The Bus...a no brainer...and touted as a great tourist convayance. (Frommers devotes nearly 3 pages to it). In the aftermath of a trasnsit strike, the prices have doubled but more important than the cost is the fact that it is a lousy way to get around. The Bus stops at every corner making trael very slow and often leaves passengers with a long walk to get to their destinations. I would avoid it at all costs planning either to stay within the confines of Waikiki, use the more expensive private Trolley or rent a car on an as needed basis keeping in mind that Honolulu traffic is among the worst I've seen anywhere in the world.But in retrospect at a great trip, the quality of the hotel and the overall characteristics of the room made a huge difference in our enjoyment of Hawaii.

<Author>KeithD61
<Content>Good and Getting Better! We just returned from a five night stay at the Radisson Waikiki (Prince Kuhio) - 4/8-13. I must say, I'm amazed at the attitude previous reviewers have had. Not one aspect of this hotel can be criticized for the price--it's a good 4-star experience and the price reflects it. For those who book on Expedia or other discount reservation engine--don't expect superior accommodations if you're paying pennies on the dollar. You don't deserve a view or a fabulous free breakfast when others are paying more for their room (we paid $150/night plus a $30 upgrade for an ocean-view room on the 35th floor). It was worth EVERY penny. Bed bugs reported by a previous reviewer must have traveled with them from home because the rooms here are impeccably clean. Being a beach hotel only means one thing--sand does get everywhere. None remained in our room after each cleaning. The continental breakfast included in our upgrade was sufficient, including fresh pineapple and mango and pastries. It was a nice start to each day of our trip. The hotel staff was very professional and helpful. As far as the total experience was concerned, the only drawback to this hotel (and it is a temporary inconvenience) is the renovation they are undergoing. As the previous reviewer states, the results will be beautiful. I was told they hope to have all renovations complete by July 1. The pool area was closed for renovation on the 12th. They were tearing out all of the pool tile and had already taken out all of the palm trees and shrubs. I can imagine that the new pool area will be spectacular when complete as the old pool area was nice as it was. In the meantime, the hotel has an agreement with another hotel across the street for guests to use their pool. But with Waikiki just steps away--who would waste his/her time sitting by a pool? Believe me when I say that I am very picky. The Radisson Waikiki is a nice hotel--and for the price is an excellent choice when visiting Honolulu. And don't miss Cheeseburger in Paradise--the food is outstanding!

<Author>mstamigirl
<Content>Better than Expected We stayed here from 3/13-3/20 and it was actually better than I expected it to be. Overall the staff was friendly and helpful and the hotel was clean and nicely decorated. They are in the middle of something like a $5 million dollar renovation so I expect it to be even better when completed. The rooms are a decent size. Our rooms had 2 double beds, which anymore everyone prefers bigger beds so ask for a bigger one if available (we didn't but next time will), but my husband said of all the hotels we stayed at these beds were the most comfortable. Our bathroom had marble floors and if spraying hairspray, etc. be careful as this makes it a little slippery. We purchased on Hotwire.com and I recommend them for most hotel purchases as we have never been disappointed. Our maid service was great  the parking attendant was very courteous. If I would have any complaints I would say get a higher room than on the second floor - somewhat noisy but not unbearable. We were also on the same floor as some of the offices maybe due to the current renovations. We never ate any meals in the hotel just because we had other things planned so can't say anything about that. There is an ABC store across the street if you need anything and most tours either pick you up at this hotel or just around the corner across the street. If you want something more centrally located this is more towards the end and you will do some walking. There is a restaurant down the street that serves breakfast for $2.75 which includes 2 eggs, 2 strips bacon, and 2 huge pancakes - very excellent! I would also recommend purchasing an Entertainment coupon book and card. We saved a lot of money with buy one get one frees and discounts. Be sure to also get all the Hawaii discount books available on most streets and compare prices. The buffet restaurant down the street on the corner was very good (sorry the name of it has left my mind). Excellent activities - Germaine Luau, Polynesian Culture Center, parasailing, Don Ho Show, Blue Hawaii Show. We even rented mopeds and toured the Island ourselves. There is a store we did not know about until the day before we left called Deiei and if you take the city bus 13 it will drop you in front of a pawn show and you cross the street go down about a block or 2 and it is on the right. We were told it is the Hawaii version of Walmart - and their prices were better than the International Market on most anything we wanted - clothing, purses, etc. If you have a room with a refrigerator or want to have some snacks in your room, go here your first day and get all the food and souveneirs you want. As far as t-shirts go they are cheaper at the market- you can get 8 for $20 in the International Market. I highly recommend this hotel and Hawaii - we will be going back in 2 years. Enjoy!  
<Date>Apr 2, 2004

<Author>SkierRobUMN
<Content>Good hotel for the money, Good location I stayed at the Radisson Prince Kuhio from March 16th - 23rd, 2004. This was my first time staying on Oahu and I didn't know what to expect so I read the reviews and this sounded like a fine hotel. I got a rate of $99 a night on Travelocity for a city view room. I got upgraded to a mountain view room upon checkin. This hotel is very clean and the renovations will be really nice when they are done. The beach is one long block away, not a bad walk (1-2 mins). ABC Convenience store right across the street has everything you could need. My only complaint about this hotel is the elevators were pretty slow. They have 5 main guest elevators (1 was out of service). During the week wait times were not too bad but on the weekends I waited upwards of 5-7 minutes for an elevator, which is suprising since the elevators are very high speed. The breakfast buffet is good if it is included in your room rate, but not worth the $15 they charge if it's not included in your room rate. The hotel is not in a shady part of waikiki, in fact I think it is a good location. Granted its not in as good a location as the Sheraton or Hyatt but still good location. I would definately stay here again if I could get a good rate but otherwise I would probably try to get a room at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider or the Hyatt Regency, they look really nice.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location 7 nights on the 15th floor, and it could not have been more perfect. Yes as others have said, the lobby is under construction, but I never heard any construction noise during my stay. This hotel is under one minute walk to the beach. A convenience store is right across the street, seconds away for all your needs. My room had a breakfast voucher included, making me think that this was going to be like all the rest of the complimentary breakfasts I have seen before at other hotels. How wrong I was, the breakfast could only be described as awesome! A wide variety of food that changes daily, from pancakes and French toast to fish, rice, salads, oatmeal, breads, muffins, cereals, and lots more. The staff was great, I stopped by the front desk during my stay several times to pick up a package, mail postcards, ask directions, get change and I was always received a big smile and warm friendly conversations. I spend a lot of time in hotels, and usually the cleaning staffs are not the friendliest if you ever deal with them, not the case here. The lady who cleaned my room was the best! The parking garage folks are super friendly and always willing to give directions or give advice for what to do and see. Not in the hotel binder, that is in the room, but is an option, is to call room service and get pizza for very reasonable; don?t forget to try the cinnapie from the pizza menu. The room was nice. The bed, mattress and pillows were top quality. Two phones and high speed internet in each room is nice. The balcony with sliding glass door was perfect, including two patio chairs. The Fridge in the room was nice for keeping beverages cool. When you walk to the beach, you will find some of the best entertainment there is just to the left before you cross the street to the beach. Most any evening you will find a group of guys playing music, they refer to themselves as Ocean Breeze. Take a few minutes to stop and listen to them. I looked forward to this every night. They play awesome Hawaiian music, but can also do most anything on request. If I have the chance to go back to Hawaii again, I will stay at this hotel again, no questions asked.

<Author>rvivian
<Content>Great hotel and location Just got back from Ohau (Feb12-20) and stayed at the prince kuhio. Staff was very friendly and helpful. The free breakfast is excellent!!! Make sure you use it as it would normally cost $15 per person. They change the food every day so it doesn't get boring. Hotel is in a perfect location. Everything was within walking distance. We stayed on the 32nd floor and the view was awesome! Parking in the hotel is $9 per day and $3 to use the in-room safe. Elevators were always available. Recommend driving the island to see everything. We had a car for the 9 days we were there and drove over 800 miles! Don't bother driving up the west side of the island as it dead ends and is dirty along the way. Try to stay off the H1 if possible as it is a traffic jam most of the day. If you are planning to go to the Arizona Memorial, get there between 7am-7:30. We got there at 7:20 and they open the doors at 7:30. We got the 8:45 tour getting there that early. It is very busy! The dole plantation is fun. Make sure you get the dole whip. Excellent! North shore is probably the best area to visit on the island. Great beaches and lots of sea turtles. There is a zoo and aquarium about 3 blocks from the hotel that are fun to go to. Make sure you get the Aloha diner's club card for $15 as there are numerous buy 1 get 1 free coupons.**********

<Content>Good hotel, Great location I just got back from a stay at the Radisson Prince Kuhio (Feb 20 -Feb 23). I found the hotel to be nice and clean, though a little dated. The hotel is currently undergoing renovation. I got a great deal through Priceline for this hotel, so I was happy with the price, location, and overall experience. Unfortunately, due to being a priceline customer, I was given a third floor room with a view of the parking garage and experienced some traffic noise. I requested a higher room (I didn't care about the view but was worried about the noise especially since there was construction going on), but they said I couldn't have a better room since I was with Priceline. It was fine. The noise wasn't bad and the price was great, so what can I say. The room itself was small, but clean. It had a small wetbar area, a minifridge, and a balcony. The blackout curtains were a nice touch. The bathroom is extremely small, really one of the smallest hotel bathrooms I have ever seen. The staff was polite and professional. The location was great. The hotel is located on Kuhio which is the street behind the main drag, Kalakaua. It is one big block (which houses the Pacific Beach hotel) from the beach. It's within walking distance to pretty much everything. It was a short walk to the zoo, Kapiolani park, Kuhio Beach park (where they do the great Sunset on the Beach nights), the Tiki Grill (get the signature salmon yum!), the international marketplace, the statue of Duke Kahanamoku where they do the torch lighting and have free entertainment, Cheeseburger in Paradise, and a couple of different shopping centers. There is also a ABC store right across the street (of course that is probably true of all the hotels since there are probably two ABC's on every block) and a McDonalds a block away (just in case you want the Hawaiian fast food breakfast of Spam, portuguese sausage, rice and eggs. The hotel is on the quieter end of Waikiki but everything seemed walkable. I walked to the Hilton Hawaiian Village with no problem. The public bus stops right across the street which is really convenient. You can take the 58 up to Diamondhead or numerous buses to Ala Moana Mall where you can transfer to a bus to North Shore or Moana Falls or a lot of different places. I took the Circle Isle bus (52) to the Pipeline and it was well worth the trip even though it took 1.5 hours. That bus also stops at numerous other North Shore destinations, the Dole Plantation, PCC, and many other places. It goes around the whole island and it only costs two bucks. Do make sure you read the destination sign on the bus and not just the route number. They have a tendency to change the routes or shorten them with little notice and they won't give you a second transfer if you need to take another bus to get to the one you originally wanted to transfer to, plus it's super inconvenient. The trolley also stops right in front of the hotel which I didn't realize until right before I left. Check out those routes. Some of them seemed more convenient and definately more scenic than the city buses. All in all, it was a great time. I definately recommend this hotel if you can get a good price, although if the prices are comparable I would probably stay at the Pacific Beach Hotel right next door. It looked really nice. Oh, and do try to do a catamaran ride. The Outrigger offers a ride on a racing catamaran that carries about 50 people. I took a sunset cruise with an open bar and sat on the nets in the front. It was fun and a beautiful ride.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Avoid the Kuhio Club rooms I booked one of the ?Prince Kuhio Club? rooms (34th floor and above) with the ocean view against my travel agents recommendations. I read several positive reviews about the 'friendly staff that is always eager to help' and about the great location of this Radisson. In my experience only the housekeeping people here were very nice, friendly and helpful. The front desk people were polite but not very friendly or anything. The overall cleanliness was good (clean towels and sheets) and the king size bed in our room was nice and firm (the way we like it). However, the rooms in this hotel are too small, the lanai?s are an afterthought to the building and are very tiny and scary, the bathrooms too are minuscule and need serious renovation (even on the club levels). The marble in the bathroom is dull and old and the toilet bowl had some cracks and stains. The rugs in the front lobby of this hotel are so worn-out that it feels depressing. For those of you going to Waikiki for the first time, or for a special occasion like anniversary or honeymoon, avoid this place. There are many decent hotels right on the beach with better and more open views of the ocean. And if you have to stay at the Radisson Prince Kuhio do not ever pay extra for their club rooms (34 ? 37 floors). They are exactly like the regular rooms (same size and decor) but are overpriced due to a free continental breakfast that is served in a small lounge area on the 37th floor and is so pathetic in quality and service that I was shocked. Please do not confuse this ?free breakfast? for the more sumptuous one served at their ?Trellises restaurant?; the one in Trellises cost $$$. Also nearby are several wonderful restaurants that would serve a nice, hot- buffet breakfast for $ 4 - $ 8. Also at the Radisson we paid about $ 9 a day for parking (this was not waived despite our club-level status)! The pool area is o.k. and the dinner buffet at Trellises was fine but pricy for the quality and the service was mediocre. The Trellises staff that hangs out in the front area needs some serious training in ?hospitality?!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good First Time in Hawaii Hotel First off, the things I wasn't crazy about: 1) There are no screens on the lanai (patio) doors. It would have been nice to have the island breeze blowing through the room, but in Hawaii, you never know what might crawl or fly into your room. 2) Room service ends at 10pm kinda early for a lively city, even if it is pretty expensive. That's really all I have in the way of negatives. My experience with the hotel was very positive, being my first time on the island. I was upgraded from a mountain view room to ocean view for free. I also had a view Diamond Head as well. The cleanliness was above average and the staff was very warm and eager to help, though now that I think about it, the only help you get with bags is from the curb to the front desk. The location of the property is great, within 15 minutes you can walk to the Public Market, any number of restaurants, shops, the zoo, Kapiolani Park (where there's free entertainment Sat and Sun evenings) and of course the beach is 3 min away. As for seeing other parts of the island, it took me about 45min to get from Waikiki to North Shore (basically furthest south, to furthest north) and about 45 min to get from Polynesian Cultural Center to Waikiki. It's less than a 20min drive to Pearl Harbor/Arizona Memorial, and the bus to the Memorial stops in front of the hotel. One tip if you're driving and heading west or trying to catch H1 (the main freeway), take the driveway directly behind the hotel when you're leaving, otherwise, you'll have to go through a series of one-way streets to get back. In the end, I paid $135@night for a very clean room with an ocean view, in Waikiki. For a 3-star property, I have no complaints and would stay here again without hesitation.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Staff The staff are the strength of this hotel - always curteous, helpful, and professional. We stayed on the 32nd floor with an ocean view which included the buffet breakfast. Great views, although if you had a room on a lower floor your view might be spoiled by a shorter hotel between the Raddison and Waikiki. The room was fine, not posh or elegant, but tastefully decorated clean and functional. Bathrooms are a bit small but no problems with the hot water or water pressure. A/C worked fine as well. Traffic noise was somewhat apparent at times but with the slider closed it was not obtrusive at all - definately quieter than most of the Waikiki hotels. It is away from the heart of Waikiki while still being a short walk away from everything.The breakfast buffet is quite excellent. This is no run-of the mill bacon and eggs deal. We had fresh fruit, polynesian sausage, eggs benedict, and more than I can list. You must try the guava-coconut syrup. Yes. it did get a little repetitive after the first four or five days, but the food was always good. We ate dinner at the Trellises once and the food was great, albeit a little pricey.As a general warning to those visiting Oahu: THEFT AND CRIME are Oahu's DIRTY LITTLE SECRET. We left our car to take a picture, locked in plain view at a beach park for less than five minutes only to have everything taken. Cash, credit cards, everything gone in just a minute or two. After talking with the police and others on the island this is becoming a MAJOR problem here. Obviously, advertising this is not good for business. Be warned.This hotel was so good in helping us out over the remaining five days of our vacation, I can't recommend them high enough. While I will likely not visit this island again, I would without reservation stay at the Raddison again. Highly recommended.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not as great as all the reviews seem to say, but entirely acceptable... We arrived through the back entrance of the Radisson on January 5, 2003. The entire front of the hotel was under construction and barricaded(quite the eyesore but the noise did not bother us one bit). First negative impression. Next, the lobby. Clean but as dated as dated could be, and the Hawaiian music we were expecting was replaced with the blaring TV at the hotel bar.The front desk staff was nice enough and we were escorted up to our room 2 hours before check in. Our oceanfront room was on the 31st floor and had wonderful views but did not have the king bed we reserved. All the hotel had left was a room with 2 doubles. Oh well.We checked out the pool area and it was adequate, but like the rest of the hotel really dated and slightly grubby. Not filthy just really in need of a facelift.The room itself was fine in size. Cleanliness was about average, however when we climbed into the bed on the first night, the sheets were COVERED WITH SAND. Frightening to think they don't change the sheets between the guests who stay at the hotel. We quickly moved to the other bed which was free of sand and the next morning laid out the sign to have the sheets changed on both beds. The shower water pressure was rotten and the toilet very hard to flush.The breakfast buffet was adequate if it is part of your package deal, but I would advise against paying the $15 per person if it is not included in your deal.The location of the hotel is quite convenient to things like Diamond Head, the Beach, shopping, restaurants, stores and public transport.In sum, for the price we paid we definitely got our money's worth. It's not a bad place and with a facelift, this could be a really lovely resort. However, the little touches that make a hotel great were missing. The staff was very nice and that's one thing that was definitely not missing.

<Author>BCBigBoy
<Content>Very nice hotel Stayed 5 nights in oceanview room on 24th floor. Nice and clean room, bathroom was a bit small but OK. Sometimes in hotels even non-smoking rooms smell, but this hotel was clean, we really liked that there was no smell whatsoever in our room or in the hallway. The hotel is one block away from the beach but still close enough, it took us about 4 minutes of slow walk to get to the beach. View was nice from 24th floor, we once had dinner on the balkony and enjoyed the sunset, beautiful! Be careful when you leave the balcony door open, there are lots of birds with no fear for humans and they just like to walk into the room and look around. Our stay included the breakfast buffet and this was excellent, lots of food and lots of fruits. There is a pool on the roof of 10th floor, quite large area and not crowded, only problem the morning sun is blocked by the hotel building. Afternoons are OK if you prefer to suntan at the pool. I would definetely stay there again, few minutes walk from the beach is not a problem and the area is quieter than right at the beach.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Stay and a Good Value After reading mostly positive reviews on this website, we booked one week at the Radisson Prince Kuhio in early November. Our travel agent upgraded us from mountain view to an ocean view room on the 31st floor for no charge.Our room was clean, comfortable and in good condition, with a nice ocean view. It was reasonably sized except for the small bathroom. Room service was consistently very good.Another perk was the daily breakfast buffet included with our package. We especially enjoyed fresh pineapple and papaya slices, along with standard hot breakfast fare and some Japanese items like white rice, mackeral and pickled sides.The balcony was an adventure. It was very small, protuding from the side of the building like an afterthought, open on three sides with a waist-high wrought iron rail. After the initial shock of looking 31 floors straight down, I got over it and enjoyed mornings out there watching life go by while doing a crossword or two. I held onto the pencil for dear life though, not wanting to surprise any pedestrians down below. The balcony was regularly visited by a variety of obviously well-fed birds.The lobby and pool areas were attractive but quiet. This is not a hotel to hang out in while watching the sunset, but there are so many good choices within walking distance, such as the ocean-front promenade, Tiki Bar  Grill at the Aston Waikiki Beach Hotel, or Banyan Court at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider. Our daily routine was to hang out along the beach until after sunset, then walk back to our quiet sanctuary a couple blocks away.I can recommend the Prince Kuhio as a good value for what you get, especially if you're looking for an upscale, quieter hotel that's still close to the beach.

<Author>TravelinGirl
<Content>Nice hotel...small, but clean  My sisters, newphews, neice and I stayed here for 2 nights (Oct 13-14, 2003). I secured our rooms thru Priceline at approx $100 per night....which I was quite excited abt. However, we were given lower floor (6th) rooms due to the pricing structure. We could have upgraded, but really didn't feel it was worth it since we didn't spend much time in the rooms except for sleeping, etc. Our rooms both had double beds and were joined together by double doors between the rooms (a plus since we're family traveling from far to see each other). The rooms were small and slightly cramped (especially with 3 large pieces of luggage in ea room, skate boards, backpacks, etc.), but they were very clean and well decorated. They were other people staying next to us, but the insulation was great because we never heard them.....just the traffic on the street below (but we kept the slider shut and the A/C on so the noise never truly bothered us). The location was superb, just a short block to Waikiki Beach and shopping (Macy's, Hermes, Tiffany's....you name it, it's there). ABC stores on every corner and McDonald's is close too (in case you have young ones clamoring for a BigMac). The hotel only charged us $10 per car per night for parking, with in and out priviledges included. Driving around Waikiki is a waste of time....best to walk and see the sights (of which there are plenty). The only drawbacks we experienced were the pool (super windy and noisy up there on the 10th floor, plus the pool bar leaves something to be desired) and the Beauty Shop (where do I begin?....no clean implements, cluttered and noisy atmosphere (TV blaring) and the chatty, nosy owner is not affilated with the hotel so no one to voice your complaint to). All in all....the hotel is nice, quiet, clean and well-suited to middle/upper-middle class clientele.....especially at $100 per night. Enjoy your vacation!!!  
<Date>Nov 10, 2003

<Author>bethrad
<Content>Very pleasantly surprised I stayed here for a long weekend after a business meeting in Honolulu. I was very pleasantly surprised - I have to admit that my expectations weren't very high, as I have stayed in some marginal Radissons. The location was good, walking distance to good shopping and about a block to the beach. I stayed on the Kuhio Club level, which is definitely worth it. My room and (ocean) view were VERY nice. My room had a small fridge, a balcony with two chairs and a small table, a wet bar/coffee maker, and furnishings appeared new, contemporary/tropical. Everything was very clean, and the staff was very friendly and helpful. There is a cafe in the hotel for inexpensive sandwiches and snacks during the day, a discounted dinner option for people dining earlier (5-7pm I think), and then a grand buffet option that is reasonable by local standards.I was very pleased with this hotel, and the rates are great for the quality of it. If you're looking for a nice, reasonably-priced hotel - this is a good bet.
